When solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle to each cautery clavile subtle, and two cauteries on the loins.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each buttock, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are either at the base, or one or more, and are old and are large humors cold and moist corrupted, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit much, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, this which is all outside below the alar bone, point to point in a triangle, and one cautery below the buttock. Two fingers;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then one puts a large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mice to all the cautery clavicle; and leave the cautery open long time. After cure the place as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut thelul, sharpen the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on that thelul cut; and leave it as long as your hand allows so the cauteries reach the birth of the vein, so that the blood stops; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointments beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting or opening, which we shall recount in its place, there comes such a sickness that can be cured only by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to any, and is filled and festering with corruption and dampness, then you must probe it with a fine probe, and make sure you know how deep the probe goes. Afterward, heat the cautery which seems like .i. razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe went in, and reheat the cautery as many times as the corrupted flesh is burned away, once, or .ij., or .iij., according to the quantity of its need; and guard against burning the nerves which are within, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestine, then guard those places, and do not make incisions beyond the flesh, and think that it is not pierced; after the cure of the place until it is healed, and if the place is sound, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is entirely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is bad, and the bone at the root is corrupted; and thus as one of these which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes as rains, and of great windiness, and does not take to a woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the reins on one side and the other with the cautery clavicle that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more great aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I make a cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as our finger; and I make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauteries be clavicle according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the marshes
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marsh is cold and moist, and does not allow for them to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it behooves one to make .iij. cauteries around the groin, as we have said of the cautery of the bladder, and .ij. cauteries on the back; and let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the bone of the hip, and for this cause it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found in the region of the lower back, then it behooves you to cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip with .i. cautery seeming like a circle, and make the mark before the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as the one used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make .iii. cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of these things that we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is in two ways: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is in many ways, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and let there be between each cautery a space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive wood; sometimes it is made cautery in the middle on top of the hip, for which reason there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do in such a manner that the circles contain the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says that the pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, on the left side a finger; and let the cauteries be cutting, and let the thickness of the heart be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, then cauterize where he feels the pain three fingers or four with the cautery which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cautery with the cutting or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so much that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do no greater nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have cauterized on the ankle of the foot, and let them until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. After a belly solution of which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in 2 parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. // And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, for this is the manner, make 1 such iron and be at the chief also as large as a thimble of finger, or a little less, and be by entrechetres and be from one entrechetres to the other with space the quantity of a fist knuckle; and be the entrechetres across two parts, and be also like nuts, and there is 1 handle of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feel it hot, and then put it on the bone of the hip diseased, and be turned on his healthy side; and cauterize once 1 cautery reont and leave it 3 days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered long times; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its harm, and rarely do we see those who use it; and nonetheless, these are good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is needed.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter spread, none of these appearances are worth cauteries, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be cleared of fetid pills or other similar things, that one makes on his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with a stylus, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see it, make three or four cauteries at the clavivial cautery medium according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to little children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight belly when they lie down, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, burn it with the cautery of this according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery scorches each part of the spine equally. And if you see it, burn around the spine with the pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be near each other. After curing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery in proximity to a nerve bundle.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints comes from humors that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the wise call “gout” properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures with medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the foot, then make the cautery to the whole cautery which one calls “point.” And if the pains come as far as the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make cauteries on each knee three or four cauteries from each part, all olive-shaped; and if you have need of more, then make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than when the tip of the heart is burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the bone two lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance to the sick person and give him medicine. For if you do good governance for him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sinew
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin and the testicles descend toward the hips, it is newly done, so when you see it being cured, that he does not move this day; and that he use things which support his belly so that the cord descends from its belly; after making him sit on his back between your hands, and commanding him to hold his arm as long as the testicles are repaired, and move them to your knees, and place a cautery below the rupture upon the bone of the hip, and all a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and he feels the heat. Then move the testicles to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return back; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put below him one cushion and one bandage on the thighs, and one other on the hip which keeps his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again another time until you arrive at the bone; and guard carefully that the testicle does not fall when you do the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or other misfortune.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and of large people also large according to their measure; after three days cure the wound with butter until the heat is gone; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie for forty days on his back until the wound is well soldered; and it is necessary that his dressings be left long, so that the boils do not come out when he wants to go into rooms.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, if he is given a good support, and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he does not work too much and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of too much braising; and when he follows this teaching he will be healed entirely. And I will say here after the treatment of tailoring in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, then you make one cautery of the cautery reont according to its quantity, and it is burned at one-third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the place of the rupture and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand in between all the cautery clamp. But the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, either from a fall or from hitting, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine doesn't work, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and of its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, it's good; if it isn't, begin another cautery on top of that one, for such is the custom that it must move to the limb that it is near, so it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	of  dislocation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Dislocations are helped at times by cautery with great help, and also the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one at the top of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the back.  And leave your hand so that the cauteries reach up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape from them; and cauterize the mice according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the meshery is spread everywhere; and it shows clearly, it behoves you to cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and 1 cautery on top of its veins, and 2 cauteries on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and 1 great one on the hip and 1 other below, and 2 on the 2 shoulders; and 2 on the knees, and 2 on the tendons of the chest, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard the nerves that are on top of the last calf, so that you do not burn them; and once it is done cauterize on the bone of the armpit, and 1 other on the bone of the stomach, and 1 other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when more cauteries are made, the more it does help, and it brings him profit; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as the healthy ones feel it, because the body is already all corrupt. And it behoves that the cauteries be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in manners of irons. After cure the place with flour of rice with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point entering into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes cautery and on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus is removed the swelling; and nonetheless let no one intervene unless he is knowledgeable of the members and of the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sickness called 'albaras' is enfeebling, and the tools of medicine are of no use, then cauterize with a cautery a point in full depth, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the discoloration is removed, and its color has changed; then cure with flour of rice and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alder, each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the spot until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a sore by fire cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a sore comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, if you cauterize it with a cautery that seems .i. circle, all around the circumference of the sore. And nonetheless the wise say that one should make cautery also in the middle of the sore; and nonetheless this does not seem to me good, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; and more righteous thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle," as we have said in a multitude of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease which is called "adubelati," and it takes time to die, or because of the superfluity that it produces, or because of the water of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see it hasten to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries, piercing it; after leave it as it is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it burn with the whole cautery, so heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this malady called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the kernel, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rot is alleviated. After the cure as long as it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of malady there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than a gangrene of a limb, for it devours the limbs as fire devours dry branches. If you see this malady in a place that can suffer cautery with fire, then sharpen the cauteries small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the malady is; after cauterize all sides as long as you reach all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, that all which is corrupted be removed. And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places softened broths with oil as long as the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption. After the cure with ointments generating flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not arise, it is good; and if it is not so, then begin again the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this gangrene has sometimes been cured by medicine aquile in place of fire cautery; but nevertheless fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of aquile medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the thorns that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that at the feet by fire a sickness arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a big thing that blunts the foot. And the cautery of this sickness is in .ij. ways. That is to say cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. Cautery of fire is that you heat .i. cautery like a feather as well as it is a vulture's plume, and let it be made of good iron to the measure that it may hold the nail on all sides, and that it have subtle margins; after this put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the base of the nail; and let it lie thus for .iij. days as long as it begins to fester; then make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with seil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment rubbing grease until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring them cautery of hot water; and is in this manner: take an iron or steel rod, or a vulture's feather, and put it on the nail and the lump, that is to say thorn, wart; and put the rod so that it encircles all around, then pour a pock of hot water onto it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the base of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep down to the root; and suffer the patient a pock the burning of the hot water an hour; then let him lie thus, and he will be uprooted from all its roots. Thus do one after another, as long as you uproot all those that are in the body, then cure them with ointments which generate grease.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or fever or other, it is necessary that you make to him four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery or weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if he will leave trembling, and hasten the health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	Of pustules painful
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At times, due to fires bathing the body, or painful pustules appear, which come from large corrupted substances. It is necessary at first when they appear that one make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that its tip be seized by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or at the lenticular cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from them onwards, but are broken the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great hemorrhages of blood occur from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grave thing to extend.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Yet nevertheless when this happens to anyone, haste to put your finger on the wound of the vein, and restrain it very much until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put on fire the olive cauteries smaller and larger as many as they are all red; then take one, or a large or small one according to the wound and its place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there as long as the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the wound is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another evil does not come upon the sick person; and know that when a vein runs out of an artery, it cannot be well stretched even if the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying with thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch blood; and be tied and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring the tightening of ligatures tightly or to put things burning upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit in any way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any medicine present, then one must put their thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is tightened above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the thumb, but apply the moist cloth frequently that be very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and tightened; and make them with the same those who need cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the illnesses for which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or hot medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of the cauteries; and I have placed this chapter from head to toe, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those who find more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason more great caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. For many kinds of people come to cures. So they come from such who have sickened so much with their illness that they die easily for the foolishness that they find in their illness, and the greatness of their malice; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is deceitful. It does not behoove that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not operate foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your sick so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and memory of length.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to those that it is before or chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the chief until the feet, for those that you may find more easily those that you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children after birth, and when the birth is too strong pulls the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a reason that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and to all that I have seen it has hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not bear it; and he believed so much the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut a wide fissure in the middle of the head; and be as long as two thumbs, as long as the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is larger, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the commissures of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not return to you: then it behooves you to cut in the middle of the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision remove the moisture entirely. After removing the incisions of fabric and powders, and put wine and oil in it, and let it so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with tents and ointments, and leave to tighten the chief bandage, and then feed the patient dry meat from little moisture as long as the limb is fortified and sound.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the size of the abscess, and its assembly of liquid; because sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess opens, and its filling of liquid, and open it according to what you are able; and guard that you do not sever the artery; and vein blood flowing so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a sickness that is called “catarrh” in the eyes or in the chest, and the sickness is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last cure is this cautery with which one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It then behooves, when you see them to cover, that the patient bend his head backwards; after, rub their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then restrain the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the vein bites, and their places are after the ears, and there they are placed; then sign their places on each side, then cover both with a sharp spatula of two parts. Until the depth comes up to the bone, and this is done through the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and cut it from above, cutting also like two thumbs across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it sends blood upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, you must measure the space of three fingers, then dig down to the bone; and what is necessary to put out the blood is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point with no syphilis, then cut it so that an abscess does not come, then strain the wound and bind it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moistures of tears and the heats in the temples and the old soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by ways of medicine and all that does not benefit him, then we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient does back the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is easily found outside than in certain men who are too cold; and if it is found, then restrain his neck the patient of some drapes, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then hold it up in height with tweezers, and depart well of the tissues that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it at the tip of the probe, then cut off that part according to the quantity of 2 fingers. For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all whole.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood of the 6 ounces, up to 3; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in 2 lengths with a strong double thread of silk so that corruption does not come before the healing of the wound, and there comes excessive bleeding; then cut off the superfluity which is between the 2 ligatures in the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize it with the cuticular cautery until the bones are reached as long as the fingers are cut; and this is the best work if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is an aid to finish the humors: for this reason it is of greater help against humors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts tents on them well made; and when they are removed, there be careful with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a cord of the artery as much as you work on it, so hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place with vitriol and constrain it with your hand that the blood stops; and if you do not have these present, put on the place your finger until the blood is frozen, and raise the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and be restrained as it is proper; and what is more mature and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenching of two parts, but the trenches be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thick, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives one should of width, and then when you have singed in the two ends, and you put the red hot iron until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two lengths; and be kept apart between the two shoulders because it is not welded with this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing down the veins that are on the forehead above the head of fury, and it does not profit medicine to be applied, and you see the face of the patient turning, and feels in the forehead a trembling as if of fever; and where oil is held and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows falls out, and the eyebrows are dried up, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it in the old days "contused cure," and you do to the patient who has this malady on their forehead make them shave so that they have no hair, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as two should all across the front going down until the nose, and the other two as two ribs above the cheeks, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries which are as two ribs above the cheeks; and move your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put in the sharp spatula two parts of which is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	of the incision which is from behind the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the two incisions to all the skin that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula fully.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if it is put in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge toward the fleshy part towards the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and put the point until it reaches the middle cut. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up to those which open at the heart, and then on the other side make in the middle cut up to the other end; and then drain the blood equally, and express the place for the taken blood; then put in each cut a tent of old cotton, and put over cloths moistened in wine and oil and asium, and keep that an abscess does not come; and on the third day untie the linen, and there administer great planting of tepid water, then the cure of basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures with which one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any come with acute catarrh, and you see the eyes watery and small, and the vision weakened, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where they are parted a sharp pain occurs, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from many veins, and the cure that there is, such is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you command the patient to raise their forehead, then make a deep incision between the eyebrow and another wide one. i. poc. And begin from the left temple incision to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the touch; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then insert between the two edges of the incision old cotton wool, and linen swabs; then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to appear, then cure it with drying things, which make cartilage grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of flower of wheat and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to prevent cartilage growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the plugging of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which goes into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or something similar as iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing thing such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone or other manner of thing which does not fit the ear nor grow in the ear falls into the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, instill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and let him sneeze with condiment, and plug his nostrils when sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. Often it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with subtle pincers, for that is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a subtle oncine of small doubleure; and if it does not come out by that, make a snare of wire and insert the head of the snare or opening into the ear forcefully, and plug what is around the snare with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter there with the snare; then pull the thing out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take some gut which they use to catch birds, and put on a small instrument which is suitable for doing this, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the gut upon the stone or whatever thing it is, and pull out forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not emerge from all these things that we have said, then you hasten to cut the ear as an abscess comes forth, and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient healthy in the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be as a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue forth, then administer i. spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist for the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with fine pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear when water falls in it is necessary for the patient to use a first-time condiment of the exterior and wide ear with old cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it goes out through this, it is good.
