If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger thin and light, and scald them a little in fire; and put them into the patient's ear one by one, and pile above with another stone on top of the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of stone in stone until all the water comes out, and thus it goes out completely; and if you see, take .i. reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch fire until the tip of the reed is burned; then make another reed as before until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body which one can feel, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the cure does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if there appears no worms, then you treat them with subtle tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the canine of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle chief into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed them throughout the whole chain; do this so often that all the worms come out. And if they don’t obey to come out, then stuff around the chain with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they don’t come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be of silver or copper, narrow below to one small holes, and above open for distilling; and for pressing inside the distillation one instrument of copper well made for that, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines in the chain, and the chain be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finished at the end of the ear; and feel the patient inside, and let the distillations be one pock heated at the fire then when it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by wound closure, or by flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes in the ear if one cannot see it; and sometimes it happens that there is i.e., a little piece of fur in the ear, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes in inside if one cannot see it, is of great healing in more dispositions, and in this one sees that you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all these spatumile from which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be aged and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or core of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, as long as that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opilation is in the ear, take one razor subtle light and it heats a little at the fire, then put it where the body of the ear. If you feel the opilation which the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce gently, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see swollen the ear, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This treatment that comes on sheets of paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry, so it is necessary to spread them with forceps and tweezers, and scrape off a spatula from their roots; then put on top of them ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it there is no decor, then cauterize it with a subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterization after the incision will be cured; and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem like gravel in its shape and in its hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hail moves from one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the wide, then the peel of each part lightly, then take as tweezers, and cut. If you can not cut without feeling a prick the paper, so nothing grieves the patient; and if the fissure is great, so assemble with a suture, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the eyes restore it soon and injures flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper, and being the hail to tweezers, and cut and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not grieve anything; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye with salty water, and cure the place of that which injures flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	This is grease which is made in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than anyone else, and grieves their eyes very much, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun for that the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces, and sleep on them, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press it at your fingers and feel the exirnach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your thigh; and then take one drape of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach of each part, then put it on top; and press with your fingers on both sides, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula sharp a fissure of the wide, and be not more great than the wound one makes at the vein; and make the leather in depth as much as you come to the exirnach; and in many dispositions comes exirnach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove then with one piece of linen cloth between your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand right and left as much as it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, that you do not come to all the spatula until the eye, that you do not bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, then carefully widen the split until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in warm and cold water, and place on top, and bandage firmly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if some men who grind herbs and put them on to corrupt the moisture that is there. Then treat it until it is healed. And if pus comes at the site, hot, then treat with soothing ointments until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born arranged other than the natural ones, and they are aged, they harm the eyes and bring many kinds of diseases like tears accustomed and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as this is cause of destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery together fire, or by medicine ague according to that it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and suture or by canes, according to that I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient on your own, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then there is brought a needle to .i. thread above; and let this be below the edge of the paper or where the hair grows near these hairs, and carry .i. thread upward to all the paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, under the hairs arranged, at all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then rule on top of the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see lift the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if to him who has need one cuts a great quantity of the paper according to that the paper is softened; then make at all the spatula above the .ij. lines that you have signed, and commence from the large tear to the small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the width of a root, then put the awl into one of the .ij. corners of the heart, then scrape it completely; then assemble the .ij. lips with a stitch of a needle to .i. thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make airdred the superfluity of the threads on the .ij. eyebrows to no sticky things, if you wish to do so; and if not, have no care about it, then leave the stitch and the threads up to .iij. days or .iiij.; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for the paper revives by the healing of the wound and the gathering together of it, but the stitch is muedre (as the ancients say), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and it is that you draw upon the paper a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at .iij. ounces according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which ascends with small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has .i. thread, and put it amidst the figure; and put .i. other thread beside the large tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above that which you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the .ij. lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then appease it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so you must use those that we have said about incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make 2 canes by art, and 2 subtle liens as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and cut the two heads of 2 parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the 2 canes of the 2 parts formed; and let it stay like this for several days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and carry, as long as it dries by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut more forces, then cure as long as it is healed; and when the wound is soldered, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the 2 canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you prick a fine needle, and put through it one thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk neatly, and tie the heads of the threads; then place the patient's head on your healthy; and be so that the work is clear because it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle into all the chase at the root of the hair adjusted, and make it pierce the paper carefully until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out from all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair sets in its place and the flesh grows on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of the natural hooves, and raise it with that one or where you leave it, as long as it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness which is called "aleacrati" or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of operating on it is that you cut open that suture and separate its lips, and put inside a tent of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not good that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form it was before; and these operations that we have said are only addresses for this illness so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness which is desoz that truly is called “axacrati,” and is natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an needle, in which it has 1 double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the threads come in 2 holes of the flesh; then are the flesh above to all the needle, and cut at 1 spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is fitting, it is good; if those are not, so take 1 razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make 2 fissures or cuts inside the paper; and let the holes of the 2 fissures be the 2 angles of the incision that you have cut, and make ones angles so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no “j. griesche”; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs is aged desoz, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the 2 parts severed, and the cuts with a thread of linen; then cure with what we have said of softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a tear or stitching or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then place between the .ij. leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip anything of all their power how they make it return the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary of work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper carefully
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering happens to the hand of a man in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the extent as the pinches, until you cut what is adhered to the spatula subtle, which is not too sharp nor too trenchant, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp or they would pierce the eye; and be your incision, by which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it heals all that assembly, and sometimes in the eye salt water, and the rise of fresh water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in an abundance of egg; and after the third day use the collyrium and the things again as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two manners: one is like .ij. hard, and one other which is not nervous, but is like white frozen moisture, and when you touch it with iron and you cauterize it with pincers, it cannot be moved; and one and the other semblance begins toward the large tear duct, and crosses poc and poc until it covers the entire view and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coils the angle with small pliers, and the essence above; then take a needle, and put on it .i. hair of horse, or cowhide, or ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a poc and insert it into the angle, and pierce it through the entire needle, and tie the angle with a thread and lift it above, and strip all the hair along the side of the angle which follows the root and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear duct with all the small spatula and as little force as possible, and leave the natural char or tear duct, so that through the incision the body of tears does not come customarily; and at any time extend the angle solely on the needle, and thread, as we have said; then strip it all over the small spatula from this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of wool crushed, and with the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as much as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not yet nerved, and you cannot push the needle, and the awl cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, operate on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail upwards subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason is quickened, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of litharge and red ointment and crushed wool, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, as long as it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess, then cauterize it and cure the abscess first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the incision and cut a part and not half so that no tear fluid comes; then instill into the eye a red colic which is made of lead white.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times with red flesh, and it covers the pupil and restrains upon the eyelids and turns them outward, and it seems like a rose of beauty; and the work for this is that the patient puts his head in good health, then he opens his eyes, and coils all that flesh with incisions suitable to these, and sustains it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting to the razor until the end, and take care that you do not wound the eye during the work; and be the incision of the spatula as we have said in the incision of the angle and the small forces of which one removes the white of the eye, as how it shapes after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silphium or distill red coral and similar corrosive medicines, and place on top the oil of fire cotton with egg white, so that it is assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the skin covers it, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do until flesh is attached to the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it behooves you to apply the cure of each weak oil of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Veins are red that are covered over the eye and take away from sight their work and weaken the eye all days. It is therefore important that you look at the eye, in which it is, whether it is inside or out, and there is no other illness besides the sebel; therefore the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your palm, then suspend those veins to the entire line according to his wisdom, and be the lines subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lines be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut other than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remaining of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning hot according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of what here is the form; and it is called "sharp head," and it is made of iron for one head reont, and it is pointed like a file as much as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two, and press your hand a little so much as you know that that corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed, and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is closed, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not a fistula, know that it is healthy; if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy than to bring back the fistula to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone the second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at 3 angles, and the shaft be tapered to the head as much as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then he places it on the bone near the tear duct, and moves his hand from the eye one palm's breadth away, then turns to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his knee; and then restores the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens its parts, then goes the matter to the knee; thus it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open entirely throughout, and there is no discharge to the knee, nor diminution, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then cleanse, then put him on suction cups or a heater without hurting so that it sucks; then place on the eye one sheet made of cotton wool and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one by four, and then place one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye has need for; then strain it from above with a hard bandage form, and recommence the suction cups so that they suck without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the sheets soften, then it is necessary that you strain it very much; then remove the sheet after the day and the night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not; then recommence the plastering and the cloths and the sheet and the suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the dislocation of cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and it comes forth full of papers like grains of resin, and it is expectable to see; therefore if you want to cover it, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the lamier part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put the other half-eyed oil in abundance of yolk; and let it stay until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape on each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes then give great appearance, pierce them with a subtle spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and bring down the eyes, and put them in immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called “alcunnati” is nothing but the socket of the eye assembled, appearing like an arrow descending, and it is not truly an arrow; and the manner of appearance of the operation is that you make the patient sit on a seat well-arranged and straight, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it as much as you see the socket coming up to your eyes; then be cautious, and do not let it descend or become dislodged the light, and have the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is an arrow, and if the descent of the socket is not arranged as we have said. so make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make on the cornea one prick following the conjunctiva with the cornea and crown, as much as the socket goes up; and when it is out, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or boiling fennel and honey, then be cured of other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the arrows of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have taken the likenesses of needles in division, and what is fitting to perceive; if in work according to the healthiness. It behooves that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie the healthy eye and restrain it firmly; then place the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eyes is left, or to your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument beside the cornea by the width of a thread in that white part of the eye to the part toward the lesser tear duct, then thrust the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and restore your hand as long as it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the hollow thing; and it behooves that the measure of the way almagda is at the full length of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal web, and then put the instrument just to where the needle is, then express it below one way after another. If the needle now descends, if the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After rest a little, and if the eye rises the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ensnared and it does not rise, withdraw almagda gently by turning your hand poco a poco; and then put back into the eye a point of seil gemme, and leave from those the oil within. Then put outside the eye the plaster or cloth moistened in rose oil and in yolk of egg, and tie with the healthy eye. Now, and those who are of our time, we put on top as a poultice with yolk of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it behooves that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit," for this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too deep into it, but make one subtle, then put almond paste, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, equip the patient with one bandage coming forward, in which he sleeps on his back in one dark place; and be deprived of all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you apply this, because the liquid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And when abscesses come, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who appease abscesses; and when it is appeased, then untie the sight and put on his face one orilliet to cover any day, and be in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and return to his affairs; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almond paste pierced, so that one sucks the liquid, but all the same I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almond, because those who do not know them see them; and be of rain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of each of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the knee
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes knee lumps are born with various shapes, because of which some appear like scorpions with many legs; and if there is such a one that has flesh that is deeply colored and another with good color. Therefore, in those of these lumps that are smooth and not deeply colored, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and place the ointment on those lumps, and rub them outwards; then cut what you can hold with a subtle sharp spatula from one side, as long as you know that the lump is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains which one cannot cover, then open it completely i.e. with instruments subtle light; so that nothing remains; and if without tear or abscess, cauterize it as is proper; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize them until the blood be extinguished and all the pus is removed, then pour on vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the opening works and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is clean. And if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh stuck in the bone above, so that instruments cannot come to cut; therefore, it behoves you to put in i.e. thread of linen a little thick, and be moistened with hands ours, and have between each knot an opening i.e., one or less; and put the patient's head of the thread into its nostril at the tip, and pull out feeling until it comes through the nostril inside the mouth; and many times do the children in schools this, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head which comes from the nostril with one hand, and the other head which comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel each after the other while those are ours which are or thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted all that flesh, then pull out the threads, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before; do this i.iii days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the nostril a band of felt for some days until it is clean, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as by which they distill the oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling a lamp open, as a band, and conduct it thus also; and if you see, then make a closed band, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease is born at the bone of birth called "telul," and it grows and becomes great after, until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and push out all the bone, then put upon its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, one should beware if it is hard, of bad color, of poor feeling: one should not touch it with iron for it is an incured abscess, for when one cuts it any time, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of bad color, and you see that one can cut all of it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry things and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, for in few men. It behooves therefore that when this happens to any, see if the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips with a suture, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and incense ground; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or other plasters, and let it stay until it dries by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's mouths there come within the lips abscesses hard, seeming to grains of seeds, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each one, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then put in the place after the incision of vitriol ground, until the blood be stanched; and then the leave of ease, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	from the root of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is born on the gums flesh knotted, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the blood run; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other powders restraining and drying; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and green as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is putrid; so you should make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do of blackness and greenish hue, and jaundice and other spots, until they are wiped out; and if one removes what there is at the first attempt, it is good; if those do not, he recommences on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments for removing, according to what the work shows, because the scraper with which one removes outside the teeth has other forms than that with which one removes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait for the drawing as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth aching. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and thinks that it is a saint's tooth, and makes him pull the good tooth; and nonetheless does not depart the pain because of this, as long as the evil one remains, for we have already seen it done to these saints; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth at all its sides; a spatula strong to ward off the gums from all parts; then move it to your two [fingers] or tweezers to the first prick and prick, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the tweezers; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After you have extracted the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and put it inside each side gently, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with a poultice, where the perforations are; and if you extract it subtly with tweezers, so that it does not break when extracting; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be well aware that you do not break it, and remain a part, and return to the patient by malice of the root greater pains than the first. And be wary that you do not do as the ignorant saints do, who by their haste and their boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and do not bring forth what we have recounted; but they bring about at times by the consequence of this great sickness for the roots that remain there, or for the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or aysil and salt; and if any bleeding comes out, which often happens, then apply the place with vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, as to how one pulls out the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and be toothed for to grip firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the pulling, then it behooves you to put on the spot a moistened cotton ball in butter, i.e., one or two days, until the sore is softened, then insert tongs that are called "algefri," because of which the jaw seems like a beak of care; and inside they should be made as well as a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because of this its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with those, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the arrangement of teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which here is the shape:
