Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not all counted; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such maladies where the old ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, or he can, then seek the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help with gestures, from this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgins, it behooves that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it nor trim it; therefore the ray; and if it is pierced with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and resembles a little beak, and be of sharpened iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope little by little in hands days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then the file of a certain form like this is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in hands days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plain at the end to all none razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness so that it be equal, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without pain, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, and this does not work; if they need to be restrained with a gold thread, because the silver thread turns green and corrodes, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too small nor too large, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are crooked, then take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the cheek between the teeth that need fixing, if there is one or more, until you wisely arrive at the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, tie it again with another thread; if it remains, and serves this way throughout its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the straightening of the two healthy teeth, and the two that need fixing, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, fresh against fresh, as we have said; and no one should intervene unless they are wise and experienced, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from a piece of bone, and it is placed in the space where there is a deficiency, and it is restrained as we have said, and it remains and serves this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to close the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament which comes below the tongue or nature itself; or by accident of a suture wound; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hands, and lift the tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knotting, and this is from the suturing of a wound, then put the probe and cut wide that ligament; and guard that the fissure be not too deeply made, for the artery which is below. And when you have done, lift the location of warm water and oil, or cold water; then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and the stitch the sick person each night, so that the place may not suture. And if bleeding comes, then put on the spot powdered vitriol; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the cautery lens-shaped, which is good for this; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rotten color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then put in the probe, and make it with a spatula subtle, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, then put on top powdered vitriol until it is scorched, then return to your work as long as you draw out all matter; then lift the location of oil and water, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come from inside the throat bumps that are called «godath», and we call them properly the .ij. almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and reddish color, then do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, then do not touch it with iron, also for the decrease of blood; but let it alone until it is ripe, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color reont, and the root is subtle, then have prepared the instrument to cover, but look first if the abscess is calm and appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his hips be in your good health, and open the mouth and take the serjans between your hands, and press the tongue below to all the instrument, from which this is the form; and be it of silver or arrain subtle as well as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and pull it upward as much as you can; and do nothing with the fabrics with it, then cut with the instrument, from which this is the form, that seems like a force; and anyway, the chief are curved, and one place the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, from which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be sharp on one side, and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and thus, and if there is evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranate fruits be cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them then like the two almonds accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say one abscess of small size; and I had well closed the entire throat so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was obstructed, and could not eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one or two days. And the abscess was raised so high that it had been put two fingers by the two openings of its birth. Then I forthwith, and placed in one a needle, then drew out the pus; and in another part a large portion of pus; then refixed another in the other opening of its birth, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I placed the needle into these abscesses, and cut a part, and there came out only a point of blood; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I incised and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and know only that God did of her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the grape is ripe and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and round, it is called "grape". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess head is calmed, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of yellow color or black, then it is necessary that you make the incision of it. For there is great danger on the patient. It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and of its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made remembrance before; then put the needle in the grape, and pull it out, and cut it at .i. of .ij. instruments that I have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds, and cure until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid to be cut, then it is necessary that you use him of something for the cauterization of the sense fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. And it is that the patient puts his head on your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confis with very live coal, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the end of this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And has or chief a hair where one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and puts the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and the mucus come from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the breast; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it being nursed and the stings of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the vein above, as long as the cotton dries on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it dry, and wait after .iiij. days or .v.. And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton wrapped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured by gargarismes until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or any of them in one pot, and put them therein, and boil; and the pot should be well glued with firm earth, and inside the pot has one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be put into the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor mounts to the boil through the tube, until the boil is mortified; after that, begin again, until the boil dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this except at the decline of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put inside its head a bit of egg shell, so that the mouth of the patient does not feel too hot; for the egg shell does not let the vapor irritate the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens to the throat bone or spine of fish, or anything else; so therefore it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and those that do not appear to you and are returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will throw out the thing dry through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one mouthful of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to its place, it will be felt, and then you will draw out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take one instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head high lifted; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to it, nor thrust in the bone; and it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, because he shall know if the thing is hoarse; if then he thrusts down, or he draws it forth equally throughout the instrument, as long as it is forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat cutting
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No times is the throat cutting medicined, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not profit, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, then that you press his tongue to the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the throat cutting, so treat it with all .i. a small probe, or subtle pincers that are good for that. And if those don't work, so take a heated hair-pointed stick, and put it into the throat of the patient, then thrust or tip of the stick .i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient remains feverish all day. Then take full .i. glass of cold water, and open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the throat cutting feels the water, so it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will come down without harming. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot where there are burning coals, and the bottom be covered with a veil pierced in the middle, and in that pierce the head of the instrument; then put your fumigation there, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes until the sinus; and the sinus will now come down, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and thus the matter is necessary that it comes down by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the sinus is, when one can see it, like tongs curved to enter into the throat; and it has the semblance of a bird's beak, and there is roughness from lime so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to those that remembrance comes after in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and in size; and it is in two ways, one being in its own semblance, and from what moisture it holds. And the second manner so is for the places where they are on the body. Because the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the boil is mature according to its accomplishment; and if there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, like abscesses near joints. Because when abscesses comes near joints, and one lets it be so for too long, perhaps the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, pierce it then as soon as it is mature; and do not pierce an abscess ripe without complete digestion accomplished, except for those near the foundation, so that it does not pour out too much, and be lengthened inside, and a fistula comes; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is mature according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where most dependent the location of the abscess, and where it opens more; and whether the piercing is long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these that swell, according to the member. And when an abscess is in its fleshy place, it is good that you let the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion completed, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be elongated from it, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and the depth of it will harden. And if any abscess which are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs. And it is necessary that you bring small incisions in small abscesses, and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become as one cloth, and is deadened, it is necessary to do as with buboes: and if there are any that are cut in three angles, and if there are any that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of angers; and if there are any where a round cut is made, and other sizes and appearing cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no head, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great bulge, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing straight away; do this many times of great to great, until the pus is all gone; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or a small child, or an old man decrepit. For the spirit trembles at any time with the exit of the pus, that perhaps the patient dies, and you do not take care. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, put tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many incisions, it is necessary that you put a tent in each one so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut out part of the skin in the abscess, and you have covered it up, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, put cold water and easily, and wet one cloth, and put it on the bleeding place many times. And if the bleeding persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book; and if it is in winter's time, and the area where the abscess is is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, it is necessary that you put cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it behoves to know universally in cures of abscesses: Or I have said how one must go before the cures of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of sores
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting on the pus-filled abscess and moist one, it is lighter because they are of little blood. And if in some of these abscesses or chief where there is no moisture, and of these fut i. abscesses that I saw or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard, rough and white stone, and cannot be broken; and if one had done any of them, one would have done to it as well as a wound with a stone. In other abscesses coming or chief, were those which come from the chief of children and from the roots of the ears, let the opening be always at the lowest point, so that pus can issue; and cure them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses appear at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other parts or body, and are numerous, and are interweaved with each other. And each scrofulous is properly within its own place, as the one and the abscess of the chief, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant who do not want to obey health. Therefore, in the one that you see of good disposition at the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not harmful to the nerves of the neck or to the artery or to the conduit, and is not too deep; then you must cut it from above, and cauterize it on each side, and open the two lips of the heart as one's needs, as we have said in abscesses of the chief; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the spatula and knife not be too deep, so that the hand does not slip, and look too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that stop blood, and hold the wound. And leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then check with your index finger if there are any small scabs left, if so, cut them and clean them. And if there is a vein in the root of the scab, it is not fitting that you cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by itself, without annoyance; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cover it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole scab, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then when there is no remaining superfluity because of the size of the scab. It is necessary that you intend to cut at the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. Those scabs that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears more; and pierce it thus as the one before mentioned, depending, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cover it with ointment encouraging flesh, as long as it is healed.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinance, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be opened; and one should not help them because all the veins and the prominences of the sick person are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the prominence, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it below three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and their throats are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the opening, then fends the skin as far as it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the channel that escapes by the place that is broken, and by the defect of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed of which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and cut all alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so long as it be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim said that one should not do this until the throat is completely constricted, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the failure of the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took one knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and well that it had not been opened a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I bandaged it, and thus I closed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not happen to the maiden but that she recovered her voice, and returned afterwards to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that in cutting into the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called “throat hernia”, and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is much in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to .ii. manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to .ii. manners, where one is similar to fat us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work of fire except in this one which is small, and the prove and seeks throughout the intromittory
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it also as our fat, and cannot to any vein, if you cut it, as we cut the others, and the train at all its edge, if there is any of it
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and encircle well throughout, and treat it as it behooves, until it be perfectly healed
des nous	of our (ones)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are ours, of which I will say all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And or it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling has not passed, and is complete the rottenness; therefore, rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With ours there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a blister, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to two appearances, or fat, or moist, and very colored as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of wounds, that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments that are called "entromissoire," according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the incision of abscesses is that you prick or moisten the place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then that it be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the entromissoire, and take care in those that jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, treat it as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so treat it in a cross and take it with forceps, and gently scrape it on each side and ward the cloth where it lies that you may draw it healthy with the new;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it returns to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it remains for a while, and the wound does not grieve, then apply to the wound some powders corrosive sharp, and tighten the wound, and put above soothing things an abscess hot, and cure with other cures until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with those who prevent flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beating is contrary to you or otherwise hurry and apply the place of powdered vitriol, and let it lie two days or three, as long as the wound rots, and rest the boiling of blood; then return to cover those that are remaining of the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the instruments inserted, and they are of three manners: large and medium and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three manners: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles with which one sews the sores, and are of citrine iron or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and are more proven to be used with black lead to encircle the curves of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the probes are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and so also there are probes that have two curves in three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and so there are probes that have three curves, and these are also in three ways; and so there are probes that have two curves, and probes of a single curve, and these are also in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these things is to cut, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we peel the skin for so that one does not cut the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the small knives put into handles so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and there are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them more than in fleshy parts such as legs, arms, breasts, and underarms, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes one makes i.e. another instrument small, seeming to the strips of fistulas, according to this form, for which one staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed sometimes in the place where there should be a cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes reopened according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like a woman's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain swollen and discolored, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to follow according to this form from this line b. until line g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and care for it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the mother's breast is laid low and softened like it happens to women, then make two incisions above in two places resembling ribs
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b to the line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the flow of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it until it dries the remaining and the fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous lumps or boils and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment beforehand as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar appearance to scrofulous ulcers, then treat it as we have said in incisions of scrofulous ulcers, and if the wound is full of pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is routed, and the skin is sutured above it, many times abscesses come about, and just as much happens with an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows this concerning the artery, then the abscess is long made by them;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your fingertips, that is to say strangulation; and when this is for the vein, then it is redness appearing beyond.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is under the armpits and groin and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and he who is in charge should also avoid it, and in him who has an inflammation of the artery made from above the skin with long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the cut as soon as possible, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, as long as it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then put a needle under it, and make it pierce to the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in 2 lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the 2 arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then stitch the place that is between the 2 links with an introducer as long as the blood that is there comes out, and make it loose the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that prevents bowing, as long as the bone hangs.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those of ointment following this, as long as it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it behooves you to grasp with your hand that which you can of the abscess to all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then thrust the needle under where you hold in your hand, and have it pierce, and there be one thread double, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or tie one of the two ends of a thread with the two ends of the shoulder;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, reinsert another needle through all of one end of the thread under the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut away the abscess as much as the excess issues, then cut away the excess from the core and leave that which is tied together;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put a moistened cloth in wine and oil on top, then administer ointments and dressings to him until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are rubbed, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these happen more often in the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints, and this is a very painful abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and is in many dispositions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when one presses it firmly, then the patient feels pain, and is not in full part of the flesh, but below the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and let it be still from all parts, and do not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered by iron: for fear it might go into contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one that is on the head or forehead, make the skin smooth with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then take some tweezers, and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook and cut away the skin, then clean out the abscess and close the wound together with stitches, and dress it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes they happen in bellies and nowhere else there is called “fungus” because of the resemblance of it, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and there are small ones and very great ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw  one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, and had fine roots, and were slightly split, and pus oozed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6,  and the work in the incision is that you look at whether the patient is moist, and the color of the arterial is white and moist and of fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the cut to the spatula is wide, and are in your presence the cautery on fire. For when cutting comes many times too great hemorrhages of blood, and if without you it is fainted, then hasten therefore to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision of iron, then take one thread of wool well made, and in tie the articulation as we have said, and let it two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of wool until it closes the articulation, and cease by it without work; and if the roots are thick, then fear to cut even for the belly, but you may well cut half,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thelul which is of reddish hue and of poor sensation and of milk appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has broken open, and I will come to the treatment of sores after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has matured
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery wound or a rupture of tissue, and it is on the belly and has no other boils, like those which happen in other wounds, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is by the rupture of the syphax and by the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its sides, it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is by moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrain at all; and if it is by blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is because of windiness, then feel the touch, and the work is that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then it is necessary that you leave the care. For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then it is necessary that you command the patient to hold his armpit, and be extended straight, then reign in a circle around the bulge;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to move sovereignly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have marked to all the spatula
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then extend the half of the abscess upward to all the large point
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the two ends be tied together;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work the half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger in it, and search for the inside;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the ligament, untie it, and put the intestine outside of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find it boiled, take it with the pincers, and cut away the excess.
