et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein goes against you, then go beautifully around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a crosswise way so that you make it perceivable;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then tighten the abscess with four threads on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave them there as long as it can, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and swollen, then cure it as it behooves, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it behooves, and close the place.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid iron cure; and let us say that an ulcer is avoided in moist places, and great caution should be taken in its cure, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the armpit, and in the groin, and similar places, and it must be entirely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge at any time the patient of black cole; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then make the patient i. good place to do the work; then set your incisions or sores, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow completely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the hemorrhage of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is extinguished; then cure him with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; thus it is illuminated only; and one must not touch iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "illuminated" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, consider if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and looseness of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient's right side with your hands, and the minister presses the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the hip, then take the spina knife according to this form: And be trenchant for 2 parts at the point, and entirely do not be so deep that it can come until the intestine when you insert it, and not pierce it.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is joined toward the intestines: If it is necessary that you cut below the belly three fingers straight above the nipple; and if the dropsy is because of the disease of the liver, then the incision should be on the left side of the belly three fingers; and if it is because of the spleen, then on the right, and it does not behoove that the patient lies upon the incision so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the whole skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand to the spina knife between the skin and the syfac as when you are scraping at the quantity of a fingernail or in length; then pierce the syfac until the spina knife comes to the place eight, and this is the place of the water, then draw out the water, and push this instrument from where it is. This form: And is similar to a silver thread subtle, and is of iron or light wood, and has in the lower part one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the chief above is the ailment, so that when the instrument comes to the eye, it descends now upon the instrument; empty therefore half or the third part, because if you empty more than it is proper in that hour, by chance the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the eye, and it is held now for the heart which stops the opening which is on the syfac, because of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin again the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering those things, and treat from the eye a small quantity;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day, and guard yourself from overflowing until there remains but a drop of eye fluid. And if you doubt about the patient, and you let out too much eye fluid, cure him with earth or hot sand, and with sweat or bath and sun, and let him drink; and cure him with drying medicines as long as he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the eye fluid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born who has no holes in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. If this is the case, it must be inspected as soon as possible with a very fine spatula according to this form: then put in the hole one clo subtil of lead, and tie it and hold it for three or four days and when he wants to make urine, let it be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and by chance it does not fit, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small, if they are medicated with the lead clo as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the hole in its place are blueish, because none are born who have the hole at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate before they raise their penis; and cannot ejaculate for that reason because the matter cannot come as far as the glans, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies usually on his back, and are the head of the rod and the cope as well as the waist of a pen, so that the pierced falls in the middle, as it convieneth; and keep yourself from overflowing of blood that often comes, and if it happens, then the stanch of those who stanch blood, and cure the wound until it is sound.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come in the rod, and it is an appearance of flesh ugly; and there are malignant and non-malignant; so it convieneth that you prick them with .i. oncine subtle, and the cope and cleans all, then put up cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is sound.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad color and suppuration, then it is necessary that you apply a cautery to it. When you have cut it, and if the boil is in the depth of the root, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the boil that is inside first; and when it is cured, then cure the outside. For when you cure it together, it is not certain that the head of the root will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come in its root and groin; so it is necessary to shave off all that is black and corrupted, then apply on the wound plaster made from the bark of quince and pomegranate, and other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauteries help with two types of conditions together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the head of the root is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you put or lead a chain of lead from the root and urinate the patient amongst; and when the skin becomes rough at the head of the root which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with one instrument until the bonds are loosened, and the head of the root is free from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a difficult thing to consider these things, then it is necessary that you scrape it with one spatula carefully from the head of the root and the skin; then gently separate between two, and put one thin cloth of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound of continuity like the others; however, when we do this work by our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the most part of masters and healers who practiced circumcision around one dal, and with force, and at all times with a new scalpel; thus it was their custom because there are two cloths, and by chance if one cuts above and remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is necessary to cover, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is with the hole of the member it is not assured; and in the purification of the elbow by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they did not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force to all the linen of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, it cuts equally in one way or the other all throughout the tension; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the rod so much, and then make him rejoice in all ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it be between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow or heart, and pull it up until the head of the shaft is in; then purify it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place signed with a double thread, then tie it below i.  one for each other lien; and hold it as ii. two by the second lieeure to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the ii. liens, then lift the heart above gently and pull the head of the shaft;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let it be corrected the blood a little and a little, because that is the cures; and put powder above and above the powder i. drapeil glued with an egg white cooked destempreit of rose water, confited with rose oil well and fresh, and let it stay there until the next day, and cure it from another cure until it is cured.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the purification is this: the two heads be held and be sharp, and be the heads also as large as the hand evenly;
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the leaves make an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce for three days, and what is below the shaft is swollen, let it be as long as the abscesses are calmed and the scabs are slightly scraped; if you can cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, heal the place of things suddenly with a wound powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut out the kernel beyond measure, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; therefore cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Urine retention is from an obstacle in the kidney, or blood that has clotted, or a bowel, or new flesh, or similar things as we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder neck, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above his back, and restrain the patient's arms as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constricted to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine light silver, like the feather of a bird; and the handle should be one palm long and a half, and finely pointed at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie at the head one pock of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe on the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the bud; then put the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient come to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conductor or where it goes is twisted; then the thread to all the wool pock and pock, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and make correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and recommence the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood comes in the bladder, or there is an assembly of rot, and you see it distilled with sharp and medicines, do as all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has .iij. openings: .ij. on one side, and .i. on the other, as you see; and the leus are shaped so that the medicine court is such that it stops the penis well without addition, so that if it can be drained the moisture, and ejected when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you want to put your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the catheter in the moisture, and draw with the drawing which is inside; so you will draw the moisture into the catheter, and then firmly reinsert the drawing inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the enema with which one enemas the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of wood, and the head is higher; and below a .i. breast or where the shoulder bone lies; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture with which you want to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed by a strong double cord, and heat .i. pock of that moisture on the fire; then put the head of the enema into the penis, then strain your hand over the bladder throughout the entire moisture administration, until the patient feels that the moisture has arrived at the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make .i. circle out of it, and pierce it roundly all around; then put .i. strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles .i. dial, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have just said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder more often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder similar to water in its subtility; and it appears harsh, and grieves the patient his penis, and he can many times, and then it enroids; and with much of these leaps the foundations are made; and it is light the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as the middle to those who are between youth and old age; and it is the cure lighter of those who have the large stone, than of those who have it small.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. Because it encumbers at times to seek the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and push them down and move them backward, so that the hips descend to the level of the bladder, and it rises no more from above; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely sloping downward; then press and touch its top.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the hip in the space, then hasten now to cut above the hip. And if it does not fall at the touch of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put it in its foundation, and press the hip, and when you feel it on your finger, say [it] to the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger and put it out further where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him that he extends with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula cuttingly, from which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between those who are between the hips and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left wing; and be straight above the stone, and the two sides be even or foundation, and let the waist be so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	For chance the press if the two sides that are or foundation, that it be pushed out without work; and know that there are such stones which have angles and margins: so is it grieved to move; and if there is one that is submerged, resembling a glint, and rounded, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that one then where it has angles and margin, make the waist greater; and if it does not come out, then you must extract it on tongs which are like a file at the top, so that it is drawn to move the stone so that it does not escape; or you thrust under it one instrument subtle curved at the top; and if you cannot engineer it thus, widen by one pock the hole, and if the stone does not come out, strain it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stones, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then drive the blade away and the small ones after, if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be carefully removed and make a larger wound. Because two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes back through the place that the skin cannot close; but nonetheless, try to drain it or break it with pliers until you pull it out in pieces
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and put on top one cloth moistened with oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then turn the patient on his back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, carefully moisten the area with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basilican ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and blood congealments in the bladder, and due to this the urine is held back, which is known in this manner that without jumping with urine: therefore you should drain in the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, so will they corrupt the bladder, and the rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound of acute and easy and slight, and help him in all the ways that you know, as long as he is healed; and it behoves that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the rod conducts, and attached within, and the urine cannot pass; so cure of these that I say then, that you enlarge it many times, it is excused from the cutting by this cure. I have already proven this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron shaped like this and have it fitted with three points on one end.
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the iron point gently into the shaft until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron in the stone back and forth, as much as you can feel the stone on the other side; soon will come the urine, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. Then it will be broken, and it will come out with the urine, and the patient will be cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of anything that hinders it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above it, then make the shaft straight with the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are present in women, and if it happens at any time, it is a serious ailment, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a woman well knowing who discovers herself to the eyes, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, so it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity requires this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and at pains the find one, and if you do not find one, then do not attempt to have one chaste maiden skilled in this; and present her to a wise woman who knows about the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her concerning the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very well if the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her down or foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she constricts it below her buttocks, and she recommends that she puts her down or with the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the con, where it is moved appeared, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her buttocks above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then put the tail in the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can possibly issue forth, and know that many ways of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have reins. If you know the appearances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone is not coming out, put crushed vitriol in place, and keep it there for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose, and have the instruments that I told you in extracting stones from people so that you can aid in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone is not coming out, and it's from the artery that was cut, put powder on the place and restrain it with strips and bandages, and do not begin again those (actions), and leave the stone and do not pull on it, for fear that the patient might die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limbs are numb, then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the under part of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called 'syfac', and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these did not have this point.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and is expanded that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, that is, long like the shape of an egg, and does not open its openings, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the openings and the white as such, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should probe with all the intro-inserter quarreit, for its shape is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to our power and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing slightly high, and put under him many blankets;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the hips;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left, and cut the skin of the hips between them from the long until near the elbow, and let your cut be straight dividing the skin of the hips until the white flesh, and the peel subtly according to your power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the  symphysis with water, to i. wide openings, and draw out all the water, then place your bandages, and hold the symphysis up; and do not touch the root of the bones, but only the symphysis; cut all or by pieces even the costal of him subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return the water.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bone leap from its place during your work, then reset it into place when you have completed the work of the symphysis; then assemble the two leaves of the root of the bones with a suture, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the bone corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the bone along with the entire suspender, and draw out the bone, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the liquid is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part as you did the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put over another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put on the two cushions, and put above cloth doubled, and tie it on top of all the linen according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and wrap them in woolen padding according to this appearance and be assembled by stitching at the neck of the breeches, and one of the heads rests on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the armpit; and the other two to the chief over the two arms, and let the whole restraint be assembled in the buckle of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this remedy of cautery is used in place of iron knife, and it is that you prick one cautery scalpel fine, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syphac containing the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syphac as one time, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salutary; and moves guarding against blood loss, and movements than the works of a knife;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing goes against you, or abscess boils or discharge of blood or other thing, so cure what is against you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then administer a puncture as I have told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the meanings that we have said that watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to all the spatula wide, and place the perforation deep into the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the water runs out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot, and tie it, and let the remaining water run out, then cure it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not let water flow into the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you pour in a quill or instrument used to treat water from dropsy, whose form is described before; and widen 1 palm's width the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after 6 months or whenever it comes together, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass the days of the patient.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this root there is fear in more positions, so it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; and it is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excessive sour and acrid humors, which are spread to the genitals, or from blows.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not feel any pain, and it is a painful abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by adventure there are some pus-filled and painful abscesses, and of a bad color, and sometimes it comes from our artery, or from an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by our artery, it is known by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press it with your hands.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it does not behoove you to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is caused by an inflammation of the vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the hands,
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well do the cutting on this sort of thing, and on other similar things.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then is the bulb on top, and the stalk towards the white part, and deliver the suspensor from all sides of the bulb.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the bulb is already softened with these new things, then it behooves you to draw out the bulb, and cut.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is airy towards the stalk, or in those which are within the vessels, then you must deliver all that vein, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or its rear, it behoves you to cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are accomplished, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then the cure of other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed in an envelope resembling a kind of onion, with the softening of the genitals
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves painfully when he goes.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure of this disease is as well prescribed as fearsome as before,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one elevated seat, then tie the suspensory of the testicles down to his two heels,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near to the penis, and the masters braid them, and they extend them.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut with a sharp trowel wide through the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle where it has one double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came from, and tie it straight to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then the knife cuts through in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupted moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then heal the wound as with the others where one avoids a bump, so that no vessel flows and nourishes one of the corners;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For by these, no harm comes, and since blood flows to all vessels, it is necessary to draw the corners to all vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the flesh does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be aided.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this branch is by the section that comes or shoulder, or the extension over the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is or of the shoulder, or of the extension of it, and these two manners of much come from causes: or of percussion, or of jumping, or of a fall, or of lifting a heavy burden, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of the shoulder, it is that it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And is the abscess even until near the center, because the pus pushes toward the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the pus, that it brings a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears various ways, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are drawn with the pus, and it is held in, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, because one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to put the intestine into its place in the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then support it on his neck between your hands, and raise his hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then extend the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the flanks long.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then put inside the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the guts can emerge.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the skin that is below the skin of the bones, until the white underlying tissue is uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your index finger into that which follows the bone, in that which is between the white tissue that is below the skin of the hoof, and between the second layer of tissue.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And depart that which is behind the hoof, and between the second layer of tissue; and then move with your right hand into the center of the bone, and keep the white tissue on top in your left hand, and raise the hoof to all the tissue toward the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the assistant to extend the hoof upward, and untie that which is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And if it has a point of the intestine enclosed or white, hard like that, and if you find none of these things, then put it into the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or one that has a thick thread made of ten threads, and put it in the back part of the scrotum, which is after the skin of the testicles; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble them one over the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the scrotum, which we have said is below the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then enclose the hairs of the threads, and tie them together forming two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except for an abscess if it comes.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put straight the thread according to the first thread long two spans of that one, and after these two threads leave the other which is under the chest of the ribs the width of a span;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the ribs, as long as the sinew and the bone, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wounds, and put the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at any time is cauterized the white fascia that we have said, after the incision, out of doubt of a flow of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the line as long as it dries through it; and if it delays in drying, then be raised with hot water, and put upon what we have said, until it dries.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is joined to the tree, in such a way that you bind the vessels after the cut above or slightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut it in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels are bleeding; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	At no time does a rupture come in the angles, as we have said, and open them; and do not pull any of the intestines to the openings, and if any are pulled out, it is bad, and repair at all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And nonetheless, if it remains too long in this point, the wound or phlegm increases, as long as the intestines are pulled out;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the fascia which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and swollen and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure this is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a wide according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the fascia which is under the skin that follows it, then take the thread and put it on top of the place appearing of the fascia;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press on the front of the belly, then count the two apparent eyes of the face above the head of the thigh, and count one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the thigh, and do not cover the face nor extend anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the root of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it by the treatment of wounds. And when you cover the threads, if you disinfect and cure the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The face is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the contents within are softened, and it becomes visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assembles the two lips with a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the sutures, and the cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the  castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that castration is common in our law, and for this reason I would like not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the skilled ones know how to respond when asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often need castration of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals. I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.  In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand, until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men: one if it is between the two sexes appears also as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. And the other manner is in women, and it has on the groin as a penis and two genitals. And the cure of the man and the woman is that you cauterize the joined parts all, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.
