Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a joined part on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. It behooves you to cut away the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or with tweezers, and do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not come from there, then treat the other wound until it is healed; and at another char that is born at the mouth of the anus, and the one employed, and by adventure falls out, and according to the resemblance of a cow, and for this reason they called it in the old days 'cow disease'. If you must cut it, as we have said about the tenting, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by illness that came to it; or it is by charm attached, or dou syfac subtle or thick, and it is made in the ribs, or in the sides, or below, or wherever; and prevents conceiving, and pregnancy, and perhaps flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the gaze of the midwife. If the obstruction is approaching appearing, if you wish a to your two or the rear. If it is dou syfac subtle, and it is approaching the .ij. pounds, then hurry, and the round thus: put your .ij. two fingers together, and the woman be on her back, legs spread; then being the .ij. pounds form, until the subtle syfac is rounded, and is over the obstruction; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the spot, and lie the woman to home each day, so that it may not move. And if the syfac is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula like a myrtle leaf. If the obstruction is of flesh born, then suspend it at the knee and cut; and have the medicines blood-stopping, as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together abundant of egg; then administer a bandage of linen wide, so that the wound may not move; and thus for a long time, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured of other cures until it is healed. And when in the ribs comes flesh born, then it is necessary to cover according to this manner, unless it is inflamed abscesses. For the inflamed abscess which is in the ribs, one must not touch to make.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those who resolve healing.  I say that hemorrhoids and the hard stuff, when they are drawn into the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, except for the cure by iron. The ones which are at the mouth of the flesh, one can feel them, are those one can cure. It behoves therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then is the hard stuff with tongs, and the cut in its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, as such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the air for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there comes a discharge of blood, so make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranate trees and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and aisil, and make .i. plaster on her back. And if she is relieved, that's good. If not, so let her apply leeches to the back and breasts without hurting; then take linen, and moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and apply it there.  And when the abscess rests, so cure its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is similar to .i. chief as sharp, if it behoves to cut it as I have said the hard stuff; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the flesh, as such as chancre and pus-filled abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more other maladies which I have said in the division. It behoves therefore that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the flesh, which is not of the abscesses that are full of pus; and if you want to know the work of iron, so regard if the abscess is beginning at its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.  Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools where he leans, and support him on his back and assemble his legs to the parts outside of the leg; and let his hips be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good linen band; then suckle his belly towards the right side, and administer the instrument which is used for opening the mouth of the flesh, because after this comes the form; and it behoves that when you see to administer this instrument, that you first stick the point in order to know the depth of the flesh, so that what goes in from the instrument does not go more deep than it should, and that it doesn't hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it behoves to cover the depth of the flesh with cloth, so that the instrument doesn't hurt him; and it behoves to put the cone of the instrument at the top, and to hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one feels it with his hand soft, then it behoves to cut it at the chief, at the spatula left; and when the pus is emptied, then it behoves that you put in the wound tentes moistened in rose oil, or in green oil sec; and put the tent further from the wound to the bottom of the flesh, and put on top of the flesh and on the bandage linen clean moistened in water or malves be cooked; then cure it after two days of ointment following this, until it is healed; and once elevate the flesh and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristolochia being cooked; then return to the ointment.  And if the wound is returned in the flesh, then it behoves that you guard yourself from cutting with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs thereof are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then hastens the child to be born; therefore you know that this childbirth is according to nature, and is the issue under its head, and the second with it; and when you see these signs, it befits gently to press her belly so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends upon its head, then does the second come with it, and it is purified of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and comes forth further the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or groin, and is turned by chance on its neck, and by other evil figures; therefore it befits the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth loudly, and the virtue of it is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and rose her nature of oil or fennel seed shall be cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the secondine and cut at its nail as long as the moisture which is in the core comes out; and take the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with muslin of fenugrec with sesame oil; then make her swallow and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: so the child will now be born. And if the two hands have come out, then it is necessary that you gently move them back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on one seat, and raise her feet up; then turn the seat over on the ground, and hold onto the woman so that she does not fall during the turning; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the knife which is before put, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the issue of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push up high.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then prick it with the point and extend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	It should jump as far as the hips, if commanded to leap, and make it sneeze from the condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it leaps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it back and forth until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, then take a mixture of alum, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the natural part of the woman inside and outside this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make him sit upright, seated until under the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened underneath, make him one collar of mire, and put it underneath, and let it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on a seat, then make him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take his belly lightly, for the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands hand over hand.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then either supporting him on his neck, and hanging the feet down, and lying on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend his hands hand over hand, and then he takes the hands above his belly, and removes the cushions underneath until it is arranged down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then he takes his feet and moves them forcefully, then he moves the belly upwards, and then he pushes his hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and he pricks the child here and there; and instructs the woman that she should be careful as long as the child is being born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child which comes out with a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise to bring back the hand
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman rise, and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot go, then make him lie on i.e., one bed, and the legs form apart
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the muscle treatment that I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on i.e., one seat, then study to return the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and guide the child according to natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to strain until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child upon his neck, and has spread her hands, and her face turned towards the back of her mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it little by little, and the egg lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, she puts it on the muscular nature of the high and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move it little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, let her sit on one seat, and command her to strain herself; and let her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to the entire shoulder
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be done in this manner to the entire shoulder, cut the shoulder with your finger, until the moisture is drained.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the child can push up on his face and neck, cut through the flesh so that it doesn't hold back, and kill the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside, until you have placed him as he should be, and command the woman that she not move at all.
adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore if it is gently straightened.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two [twins] being an odd thing, and do not live; if they are named.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are severed by the syfack that divides them, which is attached to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they issue as naturally as one under all, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue grievously, then the cure as we have said, and let the bail be subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it deserves to heal.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Never are formed in the marsh i. or ii. or iii. or iv. or v. or vi. or vii., or more up to xv., and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its wise glorious,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bailiff know all these things, because by chance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so it is done according to what is proper.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it behooves that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it behooves that the woman is laid on her back, and her shoulders are inclined downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister applies the bandage in two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it does not move with the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils with mallow and fennel and flax seed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these mucilages.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then put them gently into the mare, then take one or two of those that are suitable for these,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care if the child is born with its head rising.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If you place the needles in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or below the beard or in the groin or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	And if the descent is on feet, you place or prick it and at the middle ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And it is necessary that he hold the needle in his right hand, and put the curve between his fingers of the left hand, and thrust it with all his hand lightly, and place the needle in any one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	And this is the shape of the needle:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix it against another bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make it equal by moving it from one side to the other, so that it moves easily, and let the bones be toothed so that they hold together, as this is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then apply some of its oil to the joint, and put it in that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none remain, then put this bone or higher up its place, and do this until it all comes out fully.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be returned for constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then it is necessary that you enclose it on cloth, as long as it isses entirely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cover in the juncture of the foot or at the knife, and thus it is necessary that you do in the other hand, and for two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's shoulder is large and it is strained in the exit, or it has sharp pain assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is fitting that you put the pointed spatula between your two [bones], and make the point and extract the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	Or you put it with the instrument that is called “almidach,” so that its shape comes with the instruments or chapter which follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And in the same way, do the same if it has a large natural point.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	And then pull apart the bones with the pliers.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps out and it is strained with force, it shall be split open, as long as the moisture which is there or worse has issued forth
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot issue forth, cut it in pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it as long as the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is trapped in the belly or the breast, then you must extract it with i.e., a cloth wrapped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and press the belly or the breast, as long as the moisture inside is gone;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are dislocated and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then put his hand in through the opening of the wound, and draw it until the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then it is put one or two times, and the body will hurt
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by the heat that has come from the abscess, it does not need to be worked on
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then it is necessary to administer moist and fatty things
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can set it straight, follow what we have said about a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if you cannot do that, then treat it in pieces, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, follow what we have said about abscesses that come in the groin;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there comes discharge of blood, it should be put into a sharp ointment, and follow with other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then conceived another upon that one, and refused the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time it came to her an abscess in the bosom, and it inflamed so much that it opened, and began to great pus flow.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I pondered long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because this one whose belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I touched the wound, and in my hands were bones, as long as the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived for a long time thus, and it seemed to be a little bit of bowel from there;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recorded this chapter for anything other than that, when the masters find a strange thing, they should know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the bone to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the forceps, as it is written in the books; and to two turns as two handles of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth of the staff be i.e., two of wide, and the edge of the trees i.e., one must, and of length a palm and half.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And among the two limbs be joined to adjustments of this same staff, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm of length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the harness to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, be made of ebony or boxwood staff, according to the likeness of pliers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two shoulders two joints, as you see, of the length of one palm, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the womb with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on one bed, the feet hanging and the legs open;
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two joints together in the womb, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with the instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the womb, until the patient does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the one sees them appear, so much is the work hastened, and higher to the men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with condiment, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps because of this, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If it is not so, take one pot, and make one perforation or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calaminth, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or any of them, be boiled or put in water on the fire; then put a band or perforation in the pot and the other end in the mouth of the wound.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And let it steam until the vapors come inside the wound; then make it sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If it jumps back suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the woman to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in the juice of alder, and then put it into the wound.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And seize the second one; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the hair does not fall off during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	But you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; then it will come out and unravel.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the hair is tight, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all those things we have said, so guard that you do not use the milk.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then the enema with ointment tetra-farmacon.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she bears and puts it back, and comes forth; but nevertheless, when she bears it, bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and paleness comes to the sick woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then for fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have experienced the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one fumigates the woman at the time of childbirth and afterwards is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is shaped like a dog, and one puts the head delicate in nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be on coals, and the tinder as long as it is burning, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who don't have a perceivable foundation, but it is stopped by subtle crafts.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, it is fitting for the midwife to pierce that craft at its proper place, and not pierce it with sharp instruments, and keep the bandaging so that she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put upon it a half linen cloth in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop up, then put on a piece of lead upon the wound, and leave it for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from the closing of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closure: if it is cured, as we have said about the cauterization of flesh.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the fundament are knotted, and larger than those that come from near the external fundament or in the space of the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or more; and when that knotting is old, it works, and still moisture arises white or subtle bows,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these fistulas are pierced; and they are known by those who feel them or evacuate or venting when the patient evacuates, and perhaps some jump towards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and to half the penis; and reach up to the groin joint, and to under the hipbone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing at the base, and not piercing:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you put your two index fingers or foundation, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has a curvature, then put in a tent of fine lead, or one hair of a horse, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your fingertip;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out through the opening or windiness or vein, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce; so hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, so that urine leaks out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to its place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no torsion and the pain is inside the joint, then it is that there is a bowing in it, and there is no value of medicine or treatment by ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and the vanity of foolish remedies that intervene in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are neither persistent nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a tent of reed, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the base, then you must put your index finger there;
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then feel that the tent has pierced it; and if you discover between your finger the soft tissue or the bone, then you know that it is penetrating;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If one does not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says however that one can well heal none, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid one does, if it is that one heats up the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and it sets all hot in the fistula, as long as it comes near the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred fibers are burned, which are seeming to an eye feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of tents moistened in butter, as long as that skin is still raw, then the cure of ointment healing flesh and joining together.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it is well. If not, in no other way can it be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent goes in and does not pierce to the depth which is the foundation, and there is between your tunica and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of fascia, and you see the fistula following the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and push it forward before the tent, and then the cauterize after, as long as it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and will be delivered the tent, and will fall; then define those char faults that seem a feather of bird, and there remains nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the without-skin goes in, and is caught between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine sharp.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	Because the fire cautery assembles two good things: that is to say, the burning of those joined-up hairs, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of tents moistened in butter or in ground thing, as long as the wound lies low, and it has been burned from within by the fire;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound of eye infections by applying a hard, dry substance, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way down to the very base, and is separated from the body, then you put your finger or foundation in, and examine them.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the opening and between two is the membrane or sheath or cartilage where it is close to piercing, then there is only a way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put a tent there and care for it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not let them be too full, so that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and come the excrement by the free will of the senses.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound once it is cut near the foundation, or by tent or by another pointed instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then bind the flesh which is in the wound as well as you can
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound, and to delay the fistula in the part outside the foundation; so it is lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And at times are fistulas according to this manner: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or costs next to the foundation of along with the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And one puts two threads twisted together, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then extract the thread from that one, just as you put your two threads or foundations.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and bind them to each other, and let it be one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And restrain it every time, until the threads close the channels that are between them, and they stick together;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make for the lacing covering if it is too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatula spinal which one makes the fistula with is very acute, on one part and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because for that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to 2 manners: or they are within the fundament, as grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And there are one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and again a drop of citrine water or a drop of blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them within the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch in order to go into rooms, as long as the foundations are gone, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and can seize it with tweezers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with one drapery, or with cotton, or from a piece of felt;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and lead them to your hands, then cut them, and powder above any hot powders that are in place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then enema the patient with a harsh and biting enema to wash what is at the foundation, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient is restrained, and if the threads are far from the foundation, then the cure is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you seize them with your finger or pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of a wide width; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place upon the foundation one draping moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and place it on the foundation, and command the patient that he rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until they itch, and when they are set, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Through drying of the fevers or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of fevers in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and the medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then it is fitting that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark on top, so that it does not get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then the cure as long as it is healed as it should;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, begin the shaving again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and be scraped;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure as long as it is healed.
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formic is a small appearance faulted before the body, and goes much en by them.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And no time the trueve the cold, and it feels him also like dead of shiver, and comes in all the body, and more as hands than other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of a goose feather, or a vulture feather strong, and put that cane upon the shiver, until the circle preignite the shiver all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to all the cane until you cover all around the shiver, and let it go in by them, and root out the shiver from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do like that of a dog's iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not let it pierce, so as to hold at the two, and move pressing; And if you see this, cauterize the vein, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or copper, or melted iron or mesh; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then whom one administers care to for children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large is above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced inside; and on one side two holes, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly is where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each wound one must put a space, then put in these wounds one strong thread of twisted thread for ten or as much as it goes around, and assemble the belly as if it were a kid;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then the ligature has in front of it a strong thread, then enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and ointment the head of the enema with oil or beaten egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister squeezes it with his two hands together, until it is all in, then withdraws the enema, and raises the patient's legs to the side;
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to work well, let it stay as long as possible; and if it stays one whole night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema for the sickness of a falling belly, and the medicine rushes out quickly, let it return as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are located at the base or as an abscess, then administer the enema as subtly as for a one-year-old child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And this is the form of the subtle enema used when the skin is constrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the thrust of a stone, and the cutting of a sword or knife, or of a spear or staff or arrow, or of similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt greatly of a hot abscess: if it makes so soon to bleed from the cephalic itself even if little blood comes from the wound, and the bleeding is on the contrary side of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's intake of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his meat be lessened, and drink no wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And put on the wound, if a boil comes to it, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in wine steeped.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no boil, then put on the wound, if it is fresh and all its blood has not been shed, and it is not touched by air, a powder, which I shall say in a little while later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the art has moved it, place some ointment on it, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then assemble them by stitching, as I shall say about wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed of the bone, and hanging, and holds only by a bit, then cut it off; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat thick meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, also as beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find yourself with rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rot, and throw it away, then treat it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by anything, and it does not stop bleeding with medicines, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put into this powder which binds so that when the wound has been cleaned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly in place until it dries well and joins all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bandage it well, and leave it unbandaged if it doesn't swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime when incense or dragon's blood are not available, but that the fire has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the artist has cauterized the wound, even still, if one does not put this powder there;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but puts on certain dressings digested, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it lies bowed;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then he cares for other sores until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then he extracts it with fine pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here after the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes to the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the wound heal, and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put on the wound anything cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of these with the brain, which is the most high part of the body.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	But let the medicine be warm, such as calx washed in water and mixed with rose oil, and cupped also in water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	And other minerals according to this manner, and humid ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the head is raised and full of bulge, then pierce it or lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and there comes bleeding, then stop it, and tie it off, and cauterize it as is necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the gullet, and the passage is kept open, so that the meat goes through,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew the heart above the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural form;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the strain happens and let him for some days, then cure with ointments until he is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, so desire it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, if you can remove them all with instruments, and those that you cannot get, leave it until the wound decays;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be cleared and aligned the opening;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look if from the wound there are wind escaping as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put any powder to it in the first hour, nor bind it at all so that the blood does not stay in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And return to the heart, and console the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	But I put attractive ointment, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if no spasms come, nor bad trembling of heart nor drawing pains of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good disposition, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with bandages and other dressings, as long as it is healing;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and work, know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, so treat it as described above.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it is deep into the bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and remove the foreign objects if they are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, leave the wound to rot so that it will be easier to remove them.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And of other wounds, as of other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The displacement of the belly is great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Of the great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerve of the intestines jump out, because of which the introduction of others;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	And the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Therefore, for this reason, intestines are put back in place more carefully if they are not immediately put back in warm [water or solution]
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they go back in place more difficultly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And for this reason, it is worse to treat the middle wound because for this reason intestines are reset into place more than other two  [wounds or areas].
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to .iiij. manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The .ij. common sutures occur in the suture of the belly,
