et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	And the suture of other wounds of the body and .ij. other proper sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nonetheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has been brought out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something is to be put back in, then it is done by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook it in water with boiling and cypress and spice.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and remove the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this kind of tightening is done, and it is moved back to its place for healing.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or broth and apply bandages that are well cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by these it is aligned the entrance to small things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make an opening in the wound with the instrument that is used to treat hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the waist
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we must not cut into it without great necessity  there be;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so trench inside in the curve and not outside, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine leaps out
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is returned again according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because this moves.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and chest higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if a rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you put yourself in those that the sunken part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds put that which has appeared to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have between your hands i.e. minister pitiful who holds all the fracture to his hand
et assemble les levres;	and assemble the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound i.e., a space of, and put a needle where there is i.e., a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphon,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of the siphon the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the restraint of a double thread around the needle of two parts
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the two ends of the wound conveniently
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave one  two of spacing, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease doing this according to what you need of needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are medium-sized, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they must be shortened;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not proper to put the needles too far from the flesh and skin.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they cut and open the wound in front of the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the needles' points so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the shoulders of needles to hold them
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one needle or two are used
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you join the two joints of the skin and the two joints of the fascia together with a needle or it has one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these four joints together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle to the part where you have begun, in the manner one sews the drapes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each suture the thickness of a minor coin;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture is taken by the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that one had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was pierced by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was two palms wide of entrails
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the middle of the belly
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine after it had been for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was stitched until .xv. days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the wise men had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in one place where there were none to be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put half a handful of old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and bring it out from the outside part to the inside one;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it pierces the right core straight through, lay it on top of the siphac or where you put in the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside out;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier does furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the seam of one part, and take it up of the other, as long as the sewing is all complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of sewing, which the Galicians say properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like no other, which assemble the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the head to the other head, in such manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or head of the mirror close, and make him feel it alone,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the two heads of the syringe;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it feel from the outer part until the inner one,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	As the two shoulders of a person;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then have each one examined from the outside part to that inside, in two other shoulders of a mirror which are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common and usual way of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Gauls say this word, and no one testifies it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is more difficult to suture than other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the arrow has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then set back the intestine, and sew it up; then put on powder mixed with charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the arrow has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch up the thread, and have the sutures sealed, and the bandage.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you lack medicine, apply upon it, as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you need no other medicine in many cases when wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not join with principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is fitting that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of thyme warmed, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and lay it around the edges, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rot in the bowels, and many times it happens
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they cleanse with black wine enemas, and similarly if the rot comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "young" cannot heal when it is rotten,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And it is for the disposition of the veins that they are, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the thread jumps from the wound, put it back in as if it were an intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become dark or black, then it is necessary that you tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the bones
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads hanging from below the wound area to the outside in order to align the extraction when the bones fall and the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it may be restored in certain men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that one man was wounded or pierced in the belly of a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and through it there came excrement and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I took care of it according to what I could, and did not cease to treat it until it was healed, and the bones were soldered.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient was unwell in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they said to the experimenters that when he has a small wound in his intestine, it must be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take thread to large test (or,  thread made of big twists), then gather the lips of the wound
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that she pulls her mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then the cut the head of (or, thread around) it, and it stays so that it cannot be untied
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one other flem after in that same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If it gets hot in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can bind the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread that be much cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread i.e., a thread of fine twisted linen,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and stitch it up in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of fringes is not foreign but according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the inner parts of the bowels, there is nothing but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when it is raised and bent back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a knotted sore hard and white, in which one feels no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also raised like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it jumps clear back, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Some times little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or for its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside it, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or when the wound is festering, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	when the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is tardy for digestion, and tardy for health, and inflated by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I make you know the cure of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to where I have said, and you are confident in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it known, then take a tent of iron or iron, if the fistula is straight, otherwise curve it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then surround it with a fine tent of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for lead can be bent to follow the twisting;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula is poorly pierced by hands,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then treat it with one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully probe with your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and is it covered by a membrane,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask well the patient of the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bone be removed the rottenness and the corrupted matter which is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healed
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from right place, then you must cut it deeper, as much as you can
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist tents in medicine of honey, and push them up to the head of the fistula
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is accumulated at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointment invigorating sinews, until it is sound
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not sound by those means, then cauterize it as we have said
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves strike or injure principal members as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove all of the corruption.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with things that are appropriate until it is sound
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it does not become sound, and returns to being as before
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone far enough
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you discover and as long as you are at the bottom
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot succeed there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there isn't another thing that lets nature to do
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers.
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction with i.e. an instrument suitable for this is done
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull them all out carefully, don't leave any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture acts against you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it copes and moisture and flesh, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put upon the wound something hindering rot,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it stay until the flesh around the bones is rotten,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove only so much corruption until the blackness is entirely gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of it rotten, and comes to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it should be cleaned and covered until the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was one young man about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	As long as the materials came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and had no external cause to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	But the surgeon, through their foolishness, opened it so much that the abscess opened.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	And in pus a great deal of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and there came much of moisture that all lay swollen and wet from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mire put care for two years, and there was no sage in the art of hands
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I came to be called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those who ran through the veins to a great extent
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the body of the youth, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put a tent in one of these pits, and then I searched all the pits.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and dug into one of the pits until I uncovered a part of the bone
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came  to the inside bone
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, except for this one which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to restore the wound of soothing medicines by long length, and it cannot join.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then again I started, and discovered the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I took out the bone, and tried to join the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not more than I coped around a palm of the bone, and the treated was to its whole form
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines; and he was healed and joined together quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and he needed not to recommence the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because for bloodletting often happens, but it was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And in the place of the bone, a hard cartilage was born, and he was of good disposition and had no pain nor contrary at all, neither now nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth and strap it to the head of the bone that is broken,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command anyone to extend it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put one other linen band larger than the first one, and tie it over the skin that is now on the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh outward.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin on the place where you want to be, so that the bone does not whiten the skin;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put one coal or a board under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to be as careful as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be even more careful another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open well, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if uncover all the flesh; then put one coal under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then let it pass from one part to the other the corruption, and be the silk long of the corruption i.e. pox, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the corrupted joint, and let the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, so there is nothing else than to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is or finger of the hand, or or finger of the foot, so it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it opens to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve do not oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the scalpel and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to prepare each kind of work its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder may be dislocated due to inside, or outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you will have medicated that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by this from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the member
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb from limb
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; if you hasten to treat it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cut it, and do not allow him any space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut at the joint so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no worth of administration beyond the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus do it when the corrosion comes or sets in; if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes at any point, cut the whole part.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to death;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of covering or supporting the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend some bandages one from the lower band, and others from the upper band,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you will widen the skin which is between the two bands by one span wide, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover or cloth it, and put on each side one drape of linen, so that the sore does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And there may come to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes when you operate, cauterize the place thoroughly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put on some powders restraining there, then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackness that seemed burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it possessed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the knight saw the corruption, he hastily covered his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long afterward the corruption returned to him in the hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I put on him things  that are repulsive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he wished that I would cut off his hand, but I refused, because I had hope of repelling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and beware also if he cuts his hand, that it does not become infected
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtue of man is weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and took care to cover his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have recounted this tale for the reason that others may do likewise, if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a head in the flesh and remains for so long that it causes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then bursts and pierces, and the pus leaps out, and the wound remains open like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above it is as thin as one fine linen cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not go all the way to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it comes to the bone and penetrates it, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure of this is that you cut that skin all around, and also when it is thinned out, just like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it will not be harmed by its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you believe the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not yet complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with this enema:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the breasts are large, and the bowel within them is of a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then administer an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take thus, oil, and lead, equally, and put to boil in one vessel over a fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine becomes red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in clysters the loin, and restrain the discharge;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for 2 hours, then remove it by pressing
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is relieved and the fear is gone.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time is it clstered with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and is that you take ashes from a vine branch, and pour water over it
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then let it flow, and keep it clean, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian remedy nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then administer a clyster of water and honey where there is a bit of litharge ground;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can give them a clyster of honey and  sweet wine, as honey has the property of purifying and washing;
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes blood flow;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and you are certain that the chest is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clyster of those things which cause flesh to be born in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and is that you prepare a plaster definitive, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse him with some medicines and ointments, about which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening in the chest is small, and the cannula of the enema cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with an iron a bit, and put in an ointment tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basil ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, so much of the edge you leave it only to where the clyster can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the peritoneum that lies above is lower, so he cuts or more below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the bowel is in perfect position, then you do not let flesh interfere;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut the side below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it is arranged in such a manner that the belly reaches the lowest point that there is
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the belly is full, if one does not allow flesh to be drawn inward
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot close the breast as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it is arranged in such a manner that the belly reaches lightly downwards and nothing of the belly be left;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the chest
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and are placed on it, that is a linen cloth that covers the entire chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then they cut as forces in place the opening of the chest, that is, a bit larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then they put ointment on it (a)n other cloth according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the wound of the chest to align the ribs, and do not remove the large dressing outside except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And he who is outside the wound of the chest, often removed to remove the ribs,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know what comes from the ribs, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread out in such a manner and you see nature rise above the wound of the chest,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is already healing, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unwrap it in the morning, or every third day, and when you unwrap the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the chest does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, so do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. For there are men whose healings in their wounds take long, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a chest lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the chest does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the chest is slow to heal and is protruding, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as the ointment of diaphinit, because it has a great portion of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the ointment of diaphinit, and make it with rose oil, and the ash of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then mix it and use it; and the same thing is made with honey cooked well, mixed.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when an inflammation does not appear
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then you glue it onto one cloth, and place it over the chest, and each time administer one long thread of  aristolochia
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the lily of heaven, which is also like the flour of vetiver and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or composites: grind them, and make a powder of them, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption is already deep, and makes an impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A pimple is an abscess that arises below the finger joint of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and one does not take care of it, then there comes 1 abscess worse,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and it is worn and pulled until it reaches the root of the joint, and by chance it is worn all the way.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion comes to the bone, until it comes pain pungent, and the shoulder is of two widths, and the color is fallow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut with iron all the superfluity which is remaining from the joint,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to prick, and the blackness,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put the root under the nail that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And the end at the top, and cut that carefully and lightly
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And put on top the rest of the medicine burning and corrosive to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and treat it further, because as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the two bones are broken, then cut them in 1 of the same as has been said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and bruised, and it hurts a lot, then you must first heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the angle of the spatula knife across
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard that the tail does not come up to the flesh which is below the angle, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand's soreness
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two things that are born in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is some place where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them [bones] grow at the base of the joint, where the birth is in no one of our two arms.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in either of our two arms does not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the arm, by chance does move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of that one who is fleshy is light, in such manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the waist in its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint, he is grievous to cure; so you hold him to be covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that one who is born or should at the end of the buttocks, so you must first cut the round flesh until bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then set the bone with a suitable bandage to it, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two joints together comes from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from the burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you set that swelling, so that the parts return according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of subtle plank, until their ends are joined, as it is fitting
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If soldering comes to none of its two with the palm, then cover that solder as it is fitting.
Des vils	Of vices
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large and full of superfluous melancholy humors that come into more members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often happens in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging with syrup, and then the healthy of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is thus in .ii. manners: one is with the cup, and then draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you lift the vein, and draw it all out forcefully.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The hip is treated this way: first raise the leg with very hot water, so that the large joint is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then restrain the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut open a vein in one place, or two, or three, of a wide size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then gently elevate and pull out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it, and instruct him to keep it warm with black bread dough.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence bleeding and lancing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg for the patient is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in the bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell up;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bain, heat it at the fire, and then the cut place the vein long to the thigh or in the part below to the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin at the incision, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the root beneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then place it at the incision lightly,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then place the cup in another location above three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it to the vein, as you have done, and place it on another incision, as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then apply another cup, or more if you need them, then lift it, and place the cup on the two points of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then move it and lift it until the second incision; then extract it from one incision to the other, until all the blood has come out, then apply the cup.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and raise it, then put a needle to its full 1. very strong double thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and the tie and draw it out, and put below 1. a strait, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and guard that it does not break, for if it breaks, then one cannot draw it out or raise it, and it comes to annoyance for the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it out completely, then place upon the spot of the wound wool moistened in wine and rose oil; and tend to it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if it is necessary that you split it tortuously, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the bone is curved, and does not pierce, so that it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees are born, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes from beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it comes from within the body, from serpents and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the veins change, and the vein begins to burst forth, as does the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, then it is necessary that you envelop around a piece of wood from three and a half to two and a half inches, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and all times that it is in pain from the outside, then envelop around the wood, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it at its root, until it is fully emerged;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings an abscess and rot there, and bad sickness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for that reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the head, and nothing remains on the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is treated is 5 palms long, or 10;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And one time a worm came to me, which was 10 palms long, and when you cut it, it shoots out 1 ray or spurt, and it pierces to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of it issues forth; and let the matter which is inside be emptied, and administer to the place medicines preventing putrefaction any day, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein hands pain, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes much blood, and from which it leaps pain; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms which are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens many times to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well at the passage from limb to limb, as long as they pierce the skin where they go, and leap out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by rot of some humors, such as come worms and serpents and roundworms or belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt one of its wickedness, for when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and milked, if one can flee only when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so therefore it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong cord very tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and pull the string out, and if it is driven too deep in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if then you cauterize it with fire above until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it spoils the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, then restrain under it the eyebrow, then cut above, and the pus out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body with medicines solubles for the illnesses humors corrupted,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if a wound of flesh decaying putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called “vakirir” in our land, and is a pain that comes in certain limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen those that I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and one time after that, I saw it rise as if like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	More quickly than anything, as living silver when it departs from its place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that place, and settles in the shoulder;
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little while after it corrodes throughout the body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it returned toward her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved so from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who well moved pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I never had seen it like I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a dry body, and veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appears that constraint windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear well according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and swollen veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the  lump above and below is spread out evenly, and then cut upwards until that constraint windiness at its source is gone;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of those who bring forth wind, such as fetid pills, and pills of serpentaria, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and hairy, and joined.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those who have two angles, and those who have tongues, and those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And those which fall in any limb that falls in two ways: or in the principal member it falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you take care in the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps up the dura mater which is on top of the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when there is scotoma and soot and swirling and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without feeling in the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the wound moist white resembling to pus, and in jumping also as burned flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold off on the treatment, and treat the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the seventh moves also like the pulse, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move its root is that without pains of foam leaping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great pain and sighing; and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps it jumps from the wound any thing from the indigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and it jumps a point of fiber through the intestinal road, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.
