The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and back spine and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are saved according to various provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do it in the same way.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow that went into the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled it out from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And treat with a tool an arrow that fell in the fat of the oil under the skin.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was reshaped, and could only reach the point toward the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large of a Turkish bow, all one iron light without ears; the tool was safe, and did not bring any bad accidents to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treat an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the barbers, and subtly as I treated her, and she was healed by the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I treated an arrow to one man, that it was in his belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and I squeezed it out, and treated the wound, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man to whom an arrow fell on his back, and the wound was soldered together above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and did not change its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any inconvenience in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was soldered together;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remain thus enduring great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in one of the king's men, which was stuck in his thigh,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was a little declining toward the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat him after three days had passed. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it with a very fine probe, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on top of it an adhesive and digestive plaster because his wound did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the location of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the poultice on for several days and closed the wound directly, and the patient remained so for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow head inside his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a strong corroding medicine for several days, until it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and feel the head of the arrow which is reddening at its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pierced well the ends for about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I widened the wound so that I could insert pliers, and my own hands on either side, and it cannot be pushed out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore did not cease to contrive and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day pliers well made
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to that which its shape will come in the end of this chapter, until I worked it, and restored the wound
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and was sutured the wound, and was healed the patient completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take in everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare on things of very little importance, and on those that are present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and new instruments, to the arrangement of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not found in the limbs where they are fastened except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps further than where it enters, is an arrow that enters into the flesh, and does not leap any other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap now, let it remain until the flesh is carried around it, and the exit be healed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot move out, let it be like this for some days, and moisten it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it does not jump out, pierce around with a very fine needle until the surrounding tissues are spread open, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but let it be like this for some days until it is equal.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes as far as the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then the treatment of drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be drawn out freely, then administer poultices as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body, but it cannot be seen, then you must search the whole tent;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by the widening of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then widen it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears where it holds
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if remove the bone that is embedded in two parts as much as you can
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but draw it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then lay it until the place around it is softened, then treat it, because extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bloodletting goes against you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from incision near the nerve and the vein, and put every effort to extract the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and put the patient in the position he was in when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that there can be, and if you cannot, set it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, where one sees nothing or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees it or feels it clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then, as much as the pliers can take, and then extract it; if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it there still, and then begin to extract it again until it is drawn out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is in it, pull out the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft has broken off, and you see administering puss-drawing is necessary, then administer one instrument
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hollow of the instrument; and then pull it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, one puts one instrument to point entering within, to aid the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then cure the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the buttocks or the belly or the bladder or the ribs and it is close, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if need be.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the pointed hair is like the feather of a bird
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to put on the tip of an arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the pliers for putting and holding is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are 31 veins from which one heals, from which there are 16 chiefs.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: 2 batsons which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries which are in 2 temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and 2 veins that are in 2 tear ducts of the 2 eyes, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly used are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic and is on the inner side of the arm, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fast," and is composed of the cephalic and basilica,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the outer side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is on the bone.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is the one that is healed, which opens clearly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the  salve vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and has two veins;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot is there are three veins: one of them is below the curve of the pouch on the left side ribs;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right leg; and the vein which is called "nerves", which is in the ankle of the other leg.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are after the ears so helps with ancient catarrh, and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the sanie, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a strap.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then to your loin, and where you feel the pulse below your loin, seize hold of it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and thrust it below the vein until the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and the vein well two times through, and make blood flow as much as you see
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain it and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for ancient migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and suddenness, and habitual blepharitis, and to the body of the sharp tears the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the blood are so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And that the patient retracts his neck so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below his jaw, and then governs by it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift lightly the heart on the vein upwards to your index finger, and push the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards, and the cut, as you have done in two other veins, and make a flow of blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it together, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, as at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the vein of the forehead is as valuable as that of the cephalic vein for old face ailments, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality of this is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and steady it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it is healed and never work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper that the flames are too large; and to heal across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and to the jaw, and to the nosebleed, and to the  orifice in the eye, and to the diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some linen, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and let the healing be through the thickness, an inch long and an inch wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for fresh wounds, and for facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, even if it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his head with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle long flame, and place it in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well enough when, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not allow it to flow too much, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two guindeges helps in the treatment of the  alanne, and in the beginning of meselerie, and in many diseases, and in pestilence, and in corrodens, and in herpes, and esitiomes.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the blood is that the patient pulls his neck out from one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And so be the master standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient sitting on one seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein of the long one a little widely, then treat the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then redo the other side in the other vein, then untie the linen, and restrain all the veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of healing the limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you know them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	therefore one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you cut the larger of each side, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein below the tongue is helpful after the cephalic vein and is used for constrictions of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the vein are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he raises the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then feel both, and do not feel too deeply into them, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which commonly are felt are felt in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they prick at one entire flame, martin wide, or olive subtle as you cut trenches, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins with a flat, large blood supply, and which contain large, troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it befits the healer to heal skillfully, and that he beware of the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a gushing of blood comes, then it befits him to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it must not be piercing the flame, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not clearly open, then you should constrain it and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein from it, or you heal in its place the vein within the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the knife-flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a sharp knife.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is of the artery: escape therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spurt upwards just as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your hand on length, then remove your hand if it does not come out easily, which happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Bind the arm and leave it so, and do not move it, the patient; and be careful, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it does not come out easily, and it pains you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and bind the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a rind of fig, and break it, and take one half and tie it well up to the other day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is clean, that is good; if it is not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stanching is not done badly in more than a few positions for the small space of the wound, and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein's blood in the middle so helps that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	for those that it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is fitting for the surgeon to place himself over the nerve which is below, and if he does not prick too much, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the saintes be grieved, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men for its subtlety, so it is fitting that you feel it with the instrument annealed; and avoid the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the head so helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to vein when pricking at the olive flame or the myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and it doesn't matter if one misses the first time, and one begins again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance swells up the veins for some men, when one misses the first time, but it doesn't matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, is that it is administered only to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and it should be done in one of the three veins that are found: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent for everyone, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered to diseases does not have a determined hour, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not behoove to bleed children until fourteen years of age, nor a woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not blood let the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when certain want to bleed, in whatever manner that it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse the bowels with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If they have much phlegm held back, so that the veins do not draw up the superfluous impurities harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Do not blood let those who are too fat from meats, nor those who are drunk, as long as they are intoxicated, nor the dropsy-stricken;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it is worse after colic passion, and vomiting, and belly pain, and increase of labor in woman, and travail, and watching, and fasting, and whatever the virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly thin the humors if they are thick, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have their power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein of the wrist towards the third finger, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from labor on this day, and from pain, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyful, and let the hands of the one who is healing be higher than those who are being healed, and rub their arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then restrain the linen in the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the limb.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell and you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then place his finger of his left hand on that vein below its location one drop where he wants to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not be and fail to cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that are as thick as cords when bleeding, and some that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the flame on it, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, it is too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeons be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below where it was cut or above, if it is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the vein is inflamed and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Perhaps an abscess will come; do not put him in a bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the vein is short and subtly, and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening directly into the entire flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a point gently, so that the eyes are swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not begin bleeding again, and put on a little bit of olive oil, because it soothes the body from blood, and is well-applied in this place, the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the olive oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing applies to a three-bone fracture and a bow of them, when it is put back in place; so subtle the bone and it separates when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is only drained once when the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hasten, and put on top a sponge moistened in water and some warm wine, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is proper that you do this after the blood from the vein has flowed out, and if it remains in place after a few days with no blackening or greenish discoloration, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on no thing of aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mountain mint, or seeming.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances to the saint's basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore shun that you put on any of those things that we have said, for by adventure it comes short of the artery; but make i. plaster dry to harden the place, then cure it with other cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it behooves him who is pale and weak, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a wider wound for him, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it behooves him to bleed little by little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from the depletion of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if it is dried up, treat with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, moisten bread before bloodletting in syrup made from figs, or in honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints from bloodletting, after the outflow of blood, it is necessary that he inhale broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood within the body that is already exhausted, and brings on fever; so in this case it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in streams.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you have fulfilled all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his pulse when he is healthy, so that death may not come in place of passion
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not right when you see a person's arm dislocated and make blood flow the second time, and the wound is closed that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if he is curved, that he extends his arm fully, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it alone until it heals the second time; or you prick it at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen by the vein's exit has been expelled.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put upon it i. pinch of salt rubbed in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein of the arm is bled at the place of the vein of the neck because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the flesh is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now through the middle, not too wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if you cannot draw it out, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand in hot water, because it is put in more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the joint is crooked, and if you cut it completely through, it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep into it, because the nerves are all naked of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put your hand in hot water if it freezes in the wound, and cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and wool on the wound to soothe it, and do likewise for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood of him in the left hand is worth to the sickness of the mouse, and do all as I have said to you toward right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the sphene is worth to all the diseases that are below the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of flowers, and disease of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its blood are that the sick person puts their foot in hot water, and rubs over the vein until it softens,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many reins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so take there the larger vein, or at the ankle, where it is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you vein it on the foot, guard yourself from the nerves that are below, and cut through it as well as when cutting; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot pull out [the vein] from it, put the foot in the water and leave the vein well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first incision of the sinew is necessary, start again a little higher up because the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same with the sophen from the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the heel of the foot, and its incision relieves the pain in the hip when it is warm blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its incision are that the patient enters or bathes, and stretches above the ankle four fingers' width by twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the vein is dry, and it is very well-covered by hand humans.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then heal any vein that opens or under the foot, and toward the small toe, and ward off the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make as much blood flow as you see, then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and restrain it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of suction cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or glass, or wood; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping which is without pricking, it is done in two ways: either with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and cupping which is done by pricking and extracting blood, it is done in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely on top of the head; and the other is within the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in two ribs of the neck; and the suction under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the two shoulders; and the suction on the  hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suctions in the two arms; and the suctions on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches on the two ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except from the small veins that are spread in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it does not weaken one as much, as one does with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not fitting that it be administered, neither with hot nor cold fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness it is fitting to suction, or for customs, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and in any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such who, when they have need to blow, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who spit up phlegm and blood from their face, and their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who spit out a drop of blood from their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see through blood and gore and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed in the month, we command to ventilate after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the muse helps to the greatness of the head... which comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation is in place of the blood of the cephalic.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not fitting for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it does not become that the elderly use them, nor those who have or head colds diseases
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower because of the fear of obliviousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventosaion  in the neck is in place of the healing of the head and of the basilica, and for this reason it is worth to the treatment of the pain
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the bursting of the channel of the windpipe, and to all, and to repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there one must put not too firmly, because if it holds too tightly, it injures the belly or stomach and or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilation of the two ribs of the neck is good for pains in the head and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and you must command the patient that he squeeze his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and there does not come a running of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation below the chin is good for mouth sickness, and gum disease, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And commands the patient not to pierce them too much, for their skin is bare and contains nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The sucking cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it should be big, and of iron, that it needs to well draw; and perhaps, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The sucking cups of the legs are used openly, because they draw blood from all parts of the body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the knees, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and they are placed in the place of two shins, and of two ankles, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in more dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the sucking cup is that you put it first empty, and successively, and place it gently, and move it equally, and do not cease to do so, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the redness of the blood; then close it, and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, because there are some who have fleshy flesh, and clear pores: therefore it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a deep hole; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to strike .ii. times: the first time to subtlety the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to drain blood little by little, then we pierce only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeatedly strike; and if the vein is thick, pierce it deep, and the end is that the cords be pierced constantly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who has large pores, that you oil the places of the cupping glasses with an appetizer and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is inflamed, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbit seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is a wound, of watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one being healed has tender skin and wide pores, then it is not advisable to put any oil there,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the evacuation of water, rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, rise from ash, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or water of wheat, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not proper to cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he warms himself when he must blow wind and when he is blowing wind.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard yourself if the one who is healing is choleric, and if his veins are too full and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is necessary that he eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in the armpit, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mince puddings, and roast meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and wine with a medium scent, which is between old and new, and minced poppy, and minced rosebuds and small onions and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he shall be vented, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is fitting to give no man at any time garlic or nutmeg before or after the venting, in order to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle with the wine, but it is not fitting for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed without harming are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips and the hip, because those members do not suffer to be harmed on their own.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it only for to draw blood from limb to limb
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the groin to lessen the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an impaction or stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the impaction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it is done when it is put upon the liver and upon the mouse when there is wind detained.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these leeches are administered empty to suck only; and some times they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of tepid water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the pleura, and in this way one fills the leech with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs covenable to it have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the leech administered with fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have two inches wide and half a palm in length, and have or on the side toward the middle one small hole, as for putting a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of iron, softened in front so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a transverse bar of iron or steel, to put a candle enclosed in it,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be made both large and small according to the illnesses and the condition of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suckers of children are other than of old people, and of the thin ones than of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one thus place this sucker onto the limb?
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the candle of wax or .i. a lining, and put it within the sucker across the rod which is within the sucker,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the brightness be at the bottom of the sucker so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then put it on top of the member, and your should be on the opening that we have said so that when one wants to, one goes into vapor, and remove the suction.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And grasp the lining as before, and redo it often if you need it.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction therefore that is administered in illnesses of pleurisy, to any acute [condition], it has no shaft nor opening, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member only so long.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Bloodletting is not administered except to members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in their denuded flesh, such as the two or the like, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are that when you find bloodletting which are in clear waters without impurities, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in water, so long as they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be healthy by vein and leech, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and fall, if it is a place where one can put a leech, put it, because it does much good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the place with ease, and then with water, very well, and then bind it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the place heals too badly after the poultices, moisten one cloth of linen with cold water, and put it on, until the swelling is reduced.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the sores are multiplied, put on it ground vitriol, or saltpeter, and similar things, until it is stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	and you put on the wound half of peeled beans, and leave them there until they dry out in place, then it will now stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of these, take other bean pods.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the bean pods will not be taken, rub the wound with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until the sore issues forth.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them above, and as soon as they feel blood, they burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are weeping, powder on a bit of aloe and seed ground, or ash, they will now dry.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the matter of this chapter, they will never see in any ancient books, nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is hidden in our land, because I have never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
