And then remove the cerote, and put on the emplasters of the powder of molin with plenty of egg, then put the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be more close and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in more dispositions: whether the fracture is in one bone, or two; and restrain it above the fracture more than elsewhere, and every day less receding, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, from which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said. And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the member with hot water, until the itching is appeased; and leave the member not too tightly rest. And then resume the tightening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, so the address.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the dressings cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you soften it, that is, a little, and leave so for some days, until the dressings correct, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not unbind him until twenty days, or until he can put his hands on his neck, and be his neck equal, and take care of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty, according to the compositions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two there are few fractures, and there comes but only many times a sprain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it behooves the patient to sit crossed-legged, and be straight before him as well; then put his hand upon the board outstretched, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and place them aligned with the mirrors, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be enveloped in .i. linen drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the base near the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient to tighten it to his broken palm; and then strain with a long cloth, and be the splint of  wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and restrain it, as it behooveth.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the link between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to either of the two lower arms, if it is the elbow, set it straight as it should be; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see fit put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other arm, such as in the index finger or any of the others, set it straight, and tie it with the healthy one that is next to it; or you tie them all together in .i. holding, which is best, or put a splint on top, like an elbow; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the hot and dry abscess, and treat what comes up, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is thus one above the fracture, and one below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches each minister his limb equally; and this is when the fracture is amidst the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one limb is towards the groin, and the other limb below the fracture. And also if it is near the knee, then one limb is next to the knee, and the other extension down; then put the splint bone equally with its two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the plaster, and the tie, if an abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it be soothed then return to your work and your cure; the ligature is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap on the fracture .i.  a hard bandage doubled in .ii. or .iii., and in keep the superfluities, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put .i. long thread between the hip and the leg, near the knee below, and the head of the thread goes above; then turn back on the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the place eight between the leg and the hip of cloth soft to put equal the tightening, then begin to tie firmly .iii. or .iiii. on the fracture; and as much as it goes up from the fracture, and less tightens it; then take hold of the .ii. heads of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and tie .iii. splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it so, then k’it comes neither abscess nor inflammation nor other semblance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so untie it, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then it is necessary to extract them, if one can; and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the place, and drain pus; and cure it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no times is broken the hip thus if one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in this restoration thus made does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip joint is restored in 1 day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rut of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the rut of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is not more than a fissure, or 1 opening, and there are both wounds, and no wound, and this is well felt by all.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus done by putting equal those things which are rounded to their two sides, as long as they can be assembled and moved, then put the splint on it, and put a round piece of wood on top if needed, and restrain it as is fitting, then follow all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as a hot poultice and similar things; for each accident apply what is suitable to it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called 'mustelz' on the right and the other 'foscile'; and all fractures come as it comes to the arm, and for that reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thinner bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well; and it turns under. Then administer an extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are more pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take .ij. bandages of wool that encircle the leg on one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap in .ij. layers .i. bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, so that the leg cannot decline to the right or to the left, and thus is well; and none administer .i. splint of wool along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and place it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly this is done in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so care for it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but of the bones of the foot comes never a fracture and to two points, and there is not happened further than in more situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, put the patient on their foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then put your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their places; then put the splint and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small board to 2 fingers wide, then restrain the foot firmly, then that you have wrapped bandages and other things which you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when 3 or 4 days will have passed, untie the bandage, because you will find the bones equal, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, restore them, as we have said of the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be one pock more wide, then put under the foot that table which I have said, and strain it well; and if there are .ij. or .iij., or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in .i. piece of linen, and strain the table under the foot; and let it stand upon the top of the table far from the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to the other breaks, since we have said; and secure each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, then make her sit down enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and be held by behind; then fill the cavity of nature with cotton, and put in as much as one sto; then remove the woman, and lift her back up and down, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with the sto; and when she wants to urinate, she removes the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and thus do for seven days or so: so will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of lamb, and tie a cane to its opening, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the cane form, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand of the man or woman is broken, restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and use into it, and understand my book. For the fracture signifies more than many positions the right way of restoration: therefore understand.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the phallus; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is great, as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings that we have said witness it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, so keep the vitriol dressing, if you have no other thing, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come to it, so let the restoration wait until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it neither on the third nor fourth day, for you would make a bad accident happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on top of the uncovered heart, then it behooves you to put it in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions is not fitted for you to put it in place with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, which has .vii. or .viii.  of long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that the smith embeds .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb in your work, and let it be thicker in front and gradually thinner towards the end, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche," for which reason the curved piece should be placed on top of the visible bone; and  push once, so that it returns, and let them be equal to each other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly take hold of the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone, as long as the instrument has purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, such as a scalpel or awl, to your power; then clean what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is put back and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. Do this as long as it is in its place, then moisten one cloth in black spiced wine, and properly if it is in a joint; and do not put on the wound any cerote nor anything else where there is oil, so that it does not bring forth rot and corruption; then administer poultices once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cut away all covering around it, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times fools have done this, and brought upon the patient death or corrosion at any time; and let the straining be softer and more gentle than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it does not behoove to put on poultices; but surround it, in place of poultices, with hard cloths, and bind them. And when you see after one or two days pus emerging from the wound, remove what you have put on, and apply healing ointments for wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmacon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the member two times a day, in the morning and at evening, until it be sound and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be set apart in such a manner that the bone aligns gently below.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if each day passes, and it cannot heal but returns to its place, know that there are small pieces of bone; therefore it is necessary that you cover the wound with a tent and remove all these loose pieces which cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula arises in the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it states in its chapter before. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not treat it, because many times death comes from it, but let it be until it decays; perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then you can cure the wound, if you are able; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and a bad thing to see is the figure of the limb; and perhaps he cannot make the limb its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward then if it is fresh to us: if he administers medicines stichtics as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, as you choose any of these things, or all together, and mix them with stichic wine or with the white of egg or with oil; and place them on the wound in poultices, and hold it well, and do not loosen it by hand for a day; and then remove it, and begin another, until the swelling is gone; or you strain on a piece of well-made plank; because the property of wood is that it removes all the swelling from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and there is need to remove it, then cut above it, and make the superfluity apparent; or you reapply it to any razor until it is removed, and cure it as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and afterward the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and not properly tied as it should; or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the limb; or from too much irritation; or from too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you feed the patient well, and make his body soft, until the blood multiplies within him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and lightness; then place poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the swelling often subsides with water dressings, until the nourishment returns to the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the member twisted after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and the torture are fresh, it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of marsh mallow, and roots, and honeywort, and similar things; and make 1. a softening plaster, such as diacylon well made, and you take the marshmallow muslin, and confit it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take fig fat, and grind them with flaxseed, and medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never is removed the node by rubbing continuously and lengthily with wet hands. And be administered movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is ingrained and hardened, as stone, and needs to be removed by iron, then it is necessary to cut up to the bone, with a subtle and light incisor; and put care and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from a joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it should now be brought back without a splint.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Because if one delays, then it swells the limbs, and by chance if one sets it back with pain in place; for this reason it is not right that one moves it to the hour that it is swollen; many times brings on lameness and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, if the patient is bled, then let him be left, until the abscesses are all calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then move it gently, and cure each member as they come into their place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and the dislocations of both sides are according to .ij. manners: or they are a little bit out of their places, and softened a little; or they are dislocated entirely, and hang towards the cheek, and close the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and encloses his tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by more than one disposition.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it firmly, and do not hesitate at all;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and put his palm into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside, to make it even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the minister places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back and hurts, even if they are the two mandibles together, then apply hot water and oil, as long as they gently reset; do not delay in bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is well closed without softening, then place a soft cloth in a felt made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor does he try to chew, but eat light food until the pains are gone and the mandibles are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat lightly and do not trouble himself to open his mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well knit and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set right within an hour and are not converted to their places, then fevers and accustomed sweats come, and by chance a solution of belly, and by chance vomit pure.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these things, then know that it is perilous; and many times die those who have them within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fracture cannot dislocate from the side within the continuation of it and of the hip, and it is dislocated no time to the outside, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place firmly with his palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and the bandage, and restrain it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the bone which is toward the side cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it dislocates any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and the bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient that he rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way is brought back the bone of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is when it is dislocated to the part of the arse downward; and the second is to the part of the breast; and perhaps it is dislocated to the upper part, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and is not dislocated behind the shoulder, and not inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated downward towards the arse, especially to those who have little flesh, because in these it comes easily; to those who have enough flesh, it comes with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it carefully until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known when a dislocation is downwards towards the hip, and makes a difference between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the hip touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were one bone; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to his side, nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not amiss to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is weak.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upward, then put their fists under the seat, and lift the joint with force upward to its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upward, then put it down; so they will come gradually.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said with hands for several days afterward, then it is necessary that the sick person be bathed in hot water; and the minister should apply a softening and soothing ointment, such as decoction of aloe and fenugreek and marshmallow in water, and let it be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then be the sick person laid on their back, and put under the seat a cloth of wool even, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the sufferer on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and draw the hand of the sick person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and other ministers hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder returns all now, and if you see it so reset according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you make present i. man who is taller than the patient; and be straight towards the ribs, and put his shoulder under the seat of the patient, and lift the seat up, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and other ministers pull the hand of the patient down towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, so he leans with him something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is reset also in another manner: and is one long stick in earth, whose head be as i. pistol, and be neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then be placed below the patient, but that he has bandages on his side, and the patient is lying on the long end of the staff; then extend his hand away from the other side, and the joint will return to its place immediately.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take one splint of two arms and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded to fit into the middle under the saddle, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the head of the staff bandages underneath, so that the staff does not bruise the patient, then put it under the saddle of the patient; and extend his arm on the long end of the staff, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on one rung of a ladder of the wide, and be extended the hands down, and let the body hang down on the other side: now the joint will return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that it is, it is necessary that you put under the saddle a ball of wool even, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and auburn of an egg, on the whole shoulder and around it, then strain it under the saddle arrangement, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand to its collar, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he should not move much, as long as the limb is strengthened, because it will heal faster; and then move more after .v. days or .vij., and move it; and if it is hardened and is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cautery to three points, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the hips, and the breasts, or behind, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and it administers in another place; and care until it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain in the limb, and slowness of movement, then use the patient to bathe many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in different ways, and returns in different ways; and it has been dislocated from all sides, even front and back, and the dislocation is not well set, because one can see it well and feel it well; and dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the shoulder of the patient with the healthy one, if you look carefully. Because the joint is locked, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder to anything at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as the pus comes out of it, because if the pus did not come out, it would be painful to reset it; and perhaps it cannot be reset entirely in every way, even when it is behind; so it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and let its arms be spread, and the hands hold towards the cutting edge, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and firming the root of the palm the cutting edge which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it by two ministers, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then as you have enveloped a double cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the person of the joint joins its hand, if the oil of any eye to soften the joint, then put the joint forming, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put on a dry plaster with yolk of an egg, and the strain forming, and bend the arm to the neck of the patient, and let it for some days, then untie.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and let it be; and if you see that the joint is not well set, begin again with the plaster and the bandage, and let it be for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe it and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or put on the joint a fleece of fat sheep, then let it be for i. day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter into the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put back the bandage, and then go into the bath; and so do .ij. times or .iij., until he is healed; and if you see, so put on straw of moist chaff heated with butter, and strain over it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than the other joints However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the limb does not swell, or that an abscess comes hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reset is that you put the sick hand upon a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places it equal, so that he puts his palm upon the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, it is necessary that you look if it is well in place; then put the sick one's back of his hand upon a table to extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then put the sick one's back of his hand upon the table, and he puts his hand upon that appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then let him strain with soothing plasters of the abscesses shoes, and leave it so without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And do no harm to the patient except that as long as the hand is weak and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerve is cut or the artery; if there is no other means except to tighten with a cautery according to the case, and perhaps there is nothing else of value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then tighten it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then bathe it in hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At no time are the fingers of the hand dislocated to one side, at no time on the back of the palm or on the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore, are the fingers, and put the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and lean it towards the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it for 2 days, and then put it straight each day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and untie it each day, and make it move, and tie it again. And do this often, until it is tight;
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And also do so, if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and also do so, when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the shoulder blade on the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs of this are that the limbs jump away from their will, cannot be held, and many times are softened one limb, or both hips or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the spine moves in four parts; that which moves at the rear is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure for this is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood; there is no cure or healing of it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said manners of cures by great pronouncements, or there is not at all much profit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast beforehand, there is no sign of health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly on two sides, and one cannot cure except properly the one that comes to the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in one even place, and have a strain under him so he does not bleed.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then place one stick at the head in earth forming, and one other by the feet, and tie a linen strip under the arms of the patient, and another from the hips, knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and the minister knows the ligaments, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two joints.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the ligaments as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of 3 arms long, and put it under the arm, and the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the arm, then put the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and put the minister his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the turning tool that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you put 2 stakes at the head of the sick person's arm with a great one, and towards the feet 2 others, and have between each stake, outwards and inwards, a palm's width of long.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And have in each stake 1 pierced, where the turning comes, and let the stakes be firmly in the earth so that they do not move; and between each 2 stakes have 1 turning stake, on which the turning lies, and have in 2 turnings 2 small stakes of a palm long, to turn the turning.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the rope which is among the assels to the turning towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other turning, and each of the ministers turns his turning to the whole rope, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is evened out, he puts on a drying plaster with abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the bandaging with a tablet of 3 fingers long, which reaches the place of the rib and the part of the healthy spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until he is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if any thing comes in the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandaging that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocations; and it is the bone that opens, for which one should not have presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and not like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and poc dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the knee of the sick than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double his knee to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the swelling that is near inflamed with a hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to fever, so this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in front, so are they well his leg according to accomplishment; nevertheless, do not double knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind, so he cannot spread his knee, nor double, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and is the hip joint at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this appearance of dislocation is that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no cure; and it is not convenient that he has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocations, so you haste that you return the joint, and the extension within and without, and the movement to right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you apply one strong minister, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with one linen cloth tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands below his shoulders, then the astringent with a linen cloth on the hip; and another holds the head of the linen cloth;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend above and below all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If it is not so, it is necessary to pay attention to its resemblance. When the dislocation is at the edge, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the angle, then extend the linen upward toward the angle, and toward the force.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then seize other assistants with his arms, and embrace the large place of the affected hip, and extend it outward in this form: it will now return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the sick person together with a strong rope above the two heels, and on the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two fingers more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then be suspended by the top of a pole, and be two arms long above the ground; then command one minister that he embrace the top of the hip, and let other ministers hang with the sick person, who embrace firmly the hip, because the joint returns now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the end, let the sick person lie down, as we have said in the one who has gouty disease, and restrain one bandage on the injured leg properly, and on the foot too;
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two splints, one at the head and one at the foot, then put one splint between the hips of the patient to shape it;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have bandages of moist cloth around it so that the patient does not bleed, then extend each minister toward him, and he puts equal measures in his hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, it is good. If not, put him on a table, and press him as we said in the chapter of dislocations, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put his pain on the front of the diseased limb, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to stretch the patient down or raise him up on the earth, but rather that he be as if the hip were dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on his two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on his face, and the strap extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint to the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be in place when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; therefore adjust the thighs, and put on the splint, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and put on the splint again; and if you see that they are even, bind it as before, and let him rest for another three days; then unbind it, and allow him to walk well, as long as the limb is fortified.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he does not stop at his hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet.
